Subject: [Xitami] Preventing abuse of mailing lists
Message-ID: <43644@dsl.co.uk>

In message <EF8DD0ED6D7ED211AEF900805F77918E0807D1EF@az25exm03.geg.mot.com>
   Tran David-P94446 writes:

> This message is in MIME format. Since your mail reader does not understand
> this format, some or all of this message may not be legible.
> 
> ------_=_NextPart_000_01C11A0B.C50CAFF0
> Content-Type: text/plain;
> 	charset="iso-8859-1"
[snip]
> 
> ------_=_NextPart_000_01C11A0B.C50CAFF0
> Content-Type: application/octet-stream;
> 	name="router.net"
> Content-Transfer-Encoding: base64
> Content-Disposition: attachment;
> 	filename="router.net"
> 
[snip 269 lines of Base64 encoded information (which presumably was
originally a text file)]
> ------_=_NextPart_000_01C11A0B.C50CAFF0--
> 
> --
> Xitami Users Mailing List -- For Xitami support
> To unsubscribe: http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami
> 

There have been a number of cases of "Outlook Abuse" of late in this
mailing list.  Could I suggest to the moderator that he modifies the
mailing list software such that it scans headers for:
>   Content-Type: multipart/mixed;
or possibly even for:
>   Content-Type: multipart/*.
and rejects them by bouncing back to the originator, with a note to say
that ONLY plain ASCII text messages are acceptable for the list?

There is never any valid reason for multi-posting an article twice, in
both ASCII and HTML (except that this is the stupid configuration in
which Outlook Express and some other Windozy MUAs are set by default).
It's a hundred (thousand? whatever?) times worse for that dual-posting to
be exploded out in separate copies to every member of a mailing list.

Likewise for large enclosures/attachments: that "binary" was 24 kilobytes
long; it was exploded out a hundred- or more-fold, when whatever might be
the part of it significant to the particular problem being reported was
only a line or two long.

Understandably, there are many people nowadays who have had no tradition
of using mailing lists, and treat them as if they were one-to-one
communication with someone else on the same LAN in the office.  Sadly,
the time has long passed when these people can be educated, so it really
needs the mailing list software to step in and prevent this abuse ---
remember that in many parts of the world, people pay for every second
that they are connected on-line, and do not want to be kept on-line for
ten times as long receiving unnecessarily prolix mails full of Microsoft
bloat.

-- 
Brian {Hamilton Kelly}                                          bhk@dsl.co.uk
    "We have gone from a world of concentrated knowledge and wisdom to one of
    distributed ignorance.  And we know and understand less while being incr-
    easingly capable."              Prof. Peter Cochrane, formerly of BT Labs

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Aug  1 14:40:39 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Dan Baker)
Date: Wed, 01 Aug 2001 07:40:39 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] setting up Cisco 1720 router
References: <EF8DD0ED6D7ED211AEF900805F77918E0807D1EF@az25exm03.geg.mot.com>
Message-ID: <3B6806D7.B45897CE@dtbakerprojects.com>

first of all, this is way off topic for the xitami list, and I would
appreciate it if the thread moved to a newsgroup like comp.network....
you'll probably get more response.

Tran David-P94446 wrote:

> Hope you don't might that I emailed you. I also have the Cisco 1720 router, but I can't seem to configure it at all. This is what I did, but I can't get my PC to go to the web...
> 
> This is what I got from my internet provider....
> 
> IP: 24.177.67.129
> Submask: 255.255.255.0
> Gateway: 24.177.67.1
> 
> The router came with a build-in 10/100 Ethernet card and WAN (WIC-ENET) card which is plugged into WIC-0.
> 
> I configured the 10/100 Ethernet end to point to my local LAN (ip - 10.10.10.1), and ethenet0 to point to the outside network (cable-modem.....IP = 24.177.67.129)......
> 
> I have a private LAN with the following IP range: 10.10.10.0 --- 10.10.10.254
-------------------

I think that local LANs are expected to have the IP range 192.168.0.xxx
by default. you might try that. for the router/firewall I use the IPs
are obtained automatically with the DNS disabled, WINS using DCHP, and
no gateway defined. The router does all the work and pulls the numbers
from the ISP. 

good luck,

D

> Onderwerp: RE: [Xitami] php-files not found on server....
>
>
> At 12:46 PM 7/30/01 +0200, you wrote:
> >I am running xitami version 2.4d9 on windows98 with mysql and php. After
> >installing xitami, the perlinstaller and mysql i get  the
> message that some
> >php-files could not be located on my server. I am however very
> sure the are
> >where they should be. In the xitami archieves i found some
> messages that it
> >could be that passing unfilled variables could cause this and
> that xifusion
> >solved the problem. So i downloaded xifusion.zip.
> >
> >In the readme file in this zip, is said that during the
> installationprocess
> >a xifusion\bin dir is created with a program, later needed in the
> >installationprocess of xifusion.
>
> You are referring to the lines that say:
> PHP NOTE:  The line in the [Filter] section should look like this:
>            .php=c:\cfusion\bin\XiFusion c:\php\php.exe
>
> I assumed that XiFusion was installed in the c:\cfusion\bin directory when
> I wrote the documentation.  You have to *manually* extract
> XiFusion.exe and
> put it into a directory somewhere on your hard drive and replace
> 'c:\cfusion\bin' with the drive and directory where you put the XiFusion
> executable (XiFusion.exe).  Note that there is NO fancy install program as
> there is really only one necessary file and a 1MB installation program is
> hardly necessary for a 65K executable.
>
> BTW, this format of documentation is quite standard for DOS/Console
> programs.  DOS is simple to use, but you have to know to translate path
> names/drive letters in your head when reading readme.txt files
> since no two
> computer systems are set up exactly the same.  XiFusion is really a Win32
> Console mode program, thus I wrote the documentation using DOS
> documentation standards in mind.
>
> Also, when you start to work with web servers and interfacing CGI
> applications (which is what PHP and ColdFusion really are), knowledge of
> how to use DOS comes in quite handy.
>
>

organizations (perhaps even the FBI) might be interested in those IP
addresses).

BTW, I too have some of those requests.  I think the most harm that it
could do to Xitami servers is flood the logs :)  My server would be hard
pressed, however, to consume 5GB in logs (current free HD space)...I would
probably guess that something was happening *WAY* before Xitami would use
even 10MB.

Subject: [Xitami] Cable Modem
Message-ID: <20010802134055.89804.qmail@web10908.mail.yahoo.com>

I used to have ADSL, I now have a cable modem.  Here
is my problem...I have a two computer home network
setup.  The gateway computer is my brothers, it is
running Win98.  My computer is the client, it is
running Xitami on WinME.  When I had ADSL it worked
fine...there was a dialup of sorts with ADSL.  Now
that we have the cable modem, there is no dialup and
Xitami cannot see the ip address assign to us by the
ISP.  The configuration is as follows:

The gateway machine is running Win98, has two nic's.
One nic is connected to the cable modem, the other to
the LAN.  I have Win98's Internet Connection Sharing
working fine and I can use the printer, share files,
and get on the internet.
What do I have to do to get the client pc to see the
cable modem's ip address?  

PS-I do not have a hardware router.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug  2 18:23:23 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 02 Aug 2001 13:23:23 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] strange things
References: <3.0.6.32.20010802050448.007bb290@pop.crosswinds.net>
Message-ID: <3B698C8B.3524B715@rci.rutgers.edu>

> /default.ida?NNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNN.....

Someone discovered that if you send MS IIS webserver a VERY long packet,
the end of the packet over-writes part of the webserver code. 

The "NNNN..." is just filler. The gibberish at the end is the worm. It
corrupts part of IIS and loads the Code Red worm. See: 

   http://www.cert.org/advisories/CA-2001-23.html

There are patches for IIS that close this backdoor. 

Other webservers (including Xitami) correctly reply "Bad request" and
don't get infected. The attack is very specific to un-patched IIS
servers. It relies on both a buffer overflow and specific locations in
program memory. Even if a webserver had the buffer overflow, on non-IIS
servers the subroutines Code Red infects are not the same, nor in the
same places. 

Even though Code Red does not infest Xitami, a Code Red server anywhere
in the world can swamp the network. It appears that much of my campus
was dead-slow overnight, though I have not confirmed that it was someone
else's Code Red trying to hit us. 

> My server would be hard pressed, however, to consume 5GB in logs 

However, my WinNT machine got sluggish when I had thousands of daily
logs in one folder. 

Xitami was just a hair slow, but NT file explorer was so slow that I
finally had to bring the machine off-line (so the logs were not growing
while I was working) and copy them off to subfolders. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug  2 18:45:36 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Thu, 02 Aug 2001 12:45:36 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Cable Modem
References: <20010802134055.89804.qmail@web10908.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <3B6991C0.2C3267CE@2cah.com>

This isn't a Xitami related issue since by default Xitami listens on all
interfaces, it is a network configuration issue. ICS is one-way, outbound.

Routers are fairly cheap now days. LinkSys sells a broadband router, 4 port
switch for about $180 US that will give you everything you need. DMZ, Port
forwarding (which is what you need) and a host of other features. Or you can
look into the various software proxies that will do NAT to direct traffic to
your client.

For the money a router would be your best solution. They aren't hard to setup,
most use browser based admin.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Aug  3 16:53:41 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Joseph Saunders)
Date: Fri, 3 Aug 2001 08:53:41 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] upload
Message-ID: <64DB6640B57B4C4B97F5E2A7902494170AB3CA@cawhqexch01.caw.com>

There are perl scripts available for uploading via http.

Heres an example:

NAME
       FileUpload - Module for HTTP File Uploading.

TEST
       http://www.tneoh.zoneit.com/perl/FileUpload/form.html

SYNOPSIS
	 use strict;
	 use FileUpload;
	 use CGI qw(-private_tempfiles :standard);
	 use vars qw($q $fu);

	 $q = new CGI;
	 $fu = new FileUpload($cgi->param('ufile'));

	 # The uploaded file's size.
	 $size = $fu->size;

	 # Get the filename.
	 $filename = $fu->orig_filename;

	 # Get the full path of the file.
	 # eg result: C:\test.html
	 $filepath = $fu->orig_filepath;

	 # Get the characters allowed.
	 @chararr = $fu->allow_char;

	 # Add the characters allowed.
	 @chararr = $fu->allow_char('char1', 'char2');

	 # Get the extensions not allowed.
	 @extarr = $fu->deny_ext;

	 # Add the extensions not allowed.
	 @extarr = $fu->deny_ext('cgi', 'shtml');

	 # Save the uploaded file as the original filename.
	 $byteswritten = $fu->save;

	 # Save the uploaded file by using "newfilename".
	 $byteswritten = $fu->save_as("newfilename");

	 # Get the filehandle's current position.
	 $pos = $fu->get_pos;

	 # Set the filehandle position.
	 $fu->set_pos($newpos);

	 # Read a line.
	 $aline = $fu->get_line;

	 # Read many lines.
	 @lines = $fu->get_lines;

DESCRIPTION
       This module helps you to process uploaded file easier.

       new UPLOADEDFILE
	   UPLOADEDFILE is the value returned by CGI->param() for
	   the uploaded file.

       allow_char CHAR1, [CHAR2...]
	   CHAR1, [CHAR2...] are the characters that allowed for
	   the saved filename.	Defaults are "\w", "\-" and "\.".
	   This is using regular expression's pattern match, so
	   please check "perldoc perlre" for more details of
	   patterns defined.  Returns the array of the characters
	   allowed.

       deny_ext EXT1, [EXT2...]
	   EXT1, [EXT2...] are the extensions that the saved
	   filename can not end with. Returns the array of the
	   extensions not allowed.

       get_line
	   Read a line from the uploaded file.

       get_lines
	   Read multiple lines from the uploaded file.	Returns
	   an array of strings.

       get_pos
	   Returns the current position for uploaded file's
	   FILEHANDLE.

       orig_filename
	   Returns the original filename string.

       orig_filepath
	   Returns the filepath string, eg result: C:\test.html.

       save
	   Save the uploaded file as the original filename.
	   Returns the number of bytes actually wrote, or undef
	   if there was an error.

       save_as NEWFILEPATH
	   Save the uploaded file to the NEWFILEPATH.  Returns
	   the number of bytes actually wrote, or undef if there
	   was an error.

       set_pos POSITION
	   Set the current position of filehandle to POSITION.
	   Returns 1 upon success, 0 otherwise.

       size
	   Returns the size of the uploaded file upon success,
	   undef otherwise.

CHANGES
       0.01 -> 0.02    orig_filename() returns a wrong filename.

       0.02 -> 0.03   save_as() use read() now instead of
       sysread() to solve some reading errors.

       0.03 -> 0.04   Call the binmode() when we read and write
       for files in Win32 platforms.

DOWNLOAD
       http://www.tneoh.zoneit.com/perl/FileUpload/download/

AUTHOR
       Simon Tneoh Chee-Boon   tneohcb@pc.jaring.my

       Copyright (c) 2000 Simon Tneoh Chee-Boon. All rights
       reserved.  This program is free software; you can
       redistribute it and/or modify it under the same terms as
       Perl itself.

SEE ALSO
       CGI, IO::Handle and IO::File

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Aug  5 19:53:05 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (xitami@lists.xitami.org)
Date: Sun, 05 Aug 2001 11:53:05 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] A Hack Attempt or What?
In-Reply-To: <997037133@coconutcomm.com>
Message-ID: <997037585@coconutcomm.com>

When you say "infected" I assume that you consider it a virus - code red is
not a virus, it is just a simple command line (as seen in the log) sent to
exploit a particular security hole that exists (that is if you have not
applied the patch/fix) for Microsoft Internet Information Server (IIS) 3 and 4
I believe. So nothing has been "infected" -- at least not from the Code Red.
But watch out for the W32.Sircam.Worm@mm virus. Supposedly it only gets 98 and
ME boxes via mail readers like Outlook Express, or Outlook. You can read about
that and Code Red at http://www.sarc.com

-J

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Aug  5 23:38:43 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 06 Aug 2001 10:38:43 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] A Hack Attempt or What?
In-Reply-To: Message from GunnarSwan <GunnarSwan@altavista.com>
 of "05 Aug 2001 09:59:52 MST." <20010805165952.9693.cpmta@c012.sfo.cp.net>
Message-ID: <200108052238.KAA08397@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <20010805165952.9693.cpmta@c012.sfo.cp.net>, GunnarSwan writes:
>In my Xitami Access and Error logs, I have found the following ... this being o
>nly one of the items. There are about 5-10, all from different IP addresses.
>
>203.250.84.135 - - [04/Aug/2001:05:20:54 -0800] "GET /default.ida?NNNNNNNNNNNNN
>NNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNN
>NNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNN
>NNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNN%u9090%u6858%ucbd3%u7801%u
>9090%u6858%ucbd3%u7801%u9090%u6858%ucbd3%u7801%u9090%u9090%u8190%u00c3%u0003%u8
>b00%u531b%u53ff%u0078%u0000%u00=a%20 HTTP/1.0" 404 0 "" ""

This is the way that CodeRed (the first version) tries to spread itself.
There's also a second version (CodeRedII) which is more agressive, and
backdoors the systems it infects as well.  Both CodeRed and CodeRedII
infect only IIS (4 and 5 at least) servers via the "ida" service module;
Microsoft has had a patch out for about three weeks, but people are
still being infected by the thousands.

The requests don't affect Xitami (which just says "don't have that ida
thing"), although some other integrated webservers have apparently been
crashing due to the requests being fairly long, so there has been some
collateral damage.

I suspect it's going to take 2-3 weeks before people finally get around
to patching enough systems and this settles down.  Despite mainstream
media attention.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Aug  5 23:42:16 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 06 Aug 2001 10:42:16 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] A Hack Attempt or What?
In-Reply-To: Message from GunnarSwan <GunnarSwan@altavista.com>
 of "05 Aug 2001 11:38:40 MST." <20010805183840.17246.cpmta@c012.sfo.cp.net>
Message-ID: <200108052242.KAA08506@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <20010805183840.17246.cpmta@c012.sfo.cp.net>, GunnarSwan writes:
>[CodeRed requests]
>Again, I am running Xitami on NT set up as a bastion host.  
>Is it safe to assume that all the IP addresses in my Access and Error logs ... 
>that all those machines have been infected?

Yup.  It's the infecting machines which try to access yours with that
CodeRed (default.ida?[NX]*....) pattern, in order to infect yours (if it
was IIS -- they just try to infect, they don't check what it is first).

So yes, you're building up your very own list of infected machines.  And
if they start getting infected with CodeRedII (see, eg, Slashdot
yesterday) then they're even more at risk.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Aug  6 12:29:56 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Owen Rudge)
Date: Mon, 6 Aug 2001 12:29:56 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] xitami,php 4 and blank pages
References: <4A256AA0.00159768.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>
Message-ID: <001c01c11e6b$207d48a0$7b7d68d5@rudge>

> I know this is a common problem as I've scoured all of the mailing lists,
many
> reports of the problem but now solutions

Try copying PHP.EXE and PHP4TS.DLL to the Xitami directory and adding the
following to defaults.cfg (or whatever):

[filter]
    .php=php.exe
    .php3=php.exe
    .phtml=php.exe

This works here.

Owen Rudge
http://www.owenrudge.co.uk/
http://www.gamearchive.uk.tt/

Can you say, "Code Red"? I thought you could..

Seriously though, it is an infected system trying to infect your system via
Code Red.

1. No, not unless you want to spend all your time writing access masks.
2. They are trying to exploit a vulnerability that Xitami does not have.
3. They are trying to trigger a vulnerability in MS's IIS (v4,v5 unpatched)
that allows the virus to have SYSTEM access to your server. Since you are
running Xitami you don't have any worries.

Just to have a little fun I set up a page just for those unfortunate souls who
do get infected. Instead of returning a 404 error, Xitami on my system greets
them with a "nice" welcome. :-)

unpatched) that allows the virus to have SYSTEM access to your server.
Since you are running Xitami you don't have any worries.

Just to have a little fun I set up a page just for those unfortunate
souls who do get infected. Instead of returning a 404 error, Xitami on
my system greets them with a "nice" welcome. :-)

Eldridge Currie wrote:
> 
> Questions:
> 1. Is there anyway of keeping these people out of my system? 2. What 
> are they looking for? 3. What does "default.ida?" mean?

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Aug  6 18:41:33 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 06 Aug 2001 13:41:33 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] "default.ida?"
References: <000401c11e98$565f8f50$74504318@cybertron>
Message-ID: <3B6ED6CD.8CB0A896@rci.rutgers.edu>

> This site isn't even a very well known or popular site. 

Does not matter. This isn't SirCam that looks in Address Book and
Browser Cache for targets. 

CodeRed uses a pseudo-random number generator to pick IP numbers to hit.
It had a non-random bias, so a certain few sites got hit a LOT. But with
enough copies of CodeRed running in the world, eventually it will hit
every IP number. 

The newest mutant of CodeRed has a better number generator that is
biased towards IP numbers in the same range as the machine it is on. 

 -PRR

In message <3B6ED6CD.8CB0A896@rci.rutgers.edu> Paul Reid writes:

> The newest mutant of CodeRed has a better number generator that is
> biased towards IP numbers in the same range as the machine it is on. 

And a much more lethal payload which requires the owner of the
Microsoft-based system to reformat the hard disk and re-install, because
it leaves a nasty infection in many parts of both NT4 and Win2K.

Beware, anyone running Win2K!  Apparently if one performs a custom
install, IIS is not pre-selected for installation; but those that chose a
default install end up with a running copy of IIS.  It is many of these
systems that are getting infected at this time, which were running a web
server unbeknownst to their owners.

Of course, anyone running Xitami on port 80 will already have disabled
IIS, but some may be running both, on different ports.

[Accesslog]
    enabled=1
    filename=haccess.log
    local=1
    format=CLFX
    custom=
    translate=0
    cycle=daily
    cycle-how=rename
    cycle-time=00:00
    cycle-day=0
    cycle-size=0
    cycle-lines=0
    cycle-arg=ha%yy%mm%dd.log

I understand that I could have run a batch file to archive logs or move them

specific reasons.

> 
> Or how could create a page which would satisfy this GET request?

Create a stock HTML document and save it as 'default.ida' in the webroot for
each domain. Then in defaults.cfg add:

[MIME]
    Ida=text/html

It works here, try it:

  http://www.2cah.com/default.ida?NNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNN

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Aug  7 15:20:40 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Owen Rudge)
Date: Tue, 7 Aug 2001 15:20:40 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Code Red requests
References: <20010807140607.E279@eyup.org> <3B6FF045.77DA0D9E@2cah.com> <20010807150714.J279@eyup.org>
Message-ID: <01d401c11f4c$23f1a8a0$4d7b68d5@rudge>

> BTW is there any that XITAMI can be configured to perform a specific
> action depending on a request such "Get /default.ida..." ?
>
> Or how could create a page which would satisfy this GET request?

You could create a PHP page called default.ida with something like:

<?

mail("webmaster@$HTTP_REMOTE_HOST", "Code Red Worm", "You have been infected
by the Code Red worm! Please download the patch from www.microsoft.com.",
"From: You <you@yourdomain.com>\n");

// please note this script is untested
?>

and add .ida = php.exe in the [Filters] section of defaults.cfg. Or you
could create a Perl script and set the filter up to run Perl instead of PHP.

http://www.owenrudge.co.uk/
http://www.gamearchive.uk.tt/

denail-of-service attacks.

"Owen Rudge" <owen@osplus.co.uk> on 06/08/2001 09:29:56 PM

> I know this is a common problem as I've scoured all of the mailing lists,
many
> reports of the problem but now solutions

Try copying PHP.EXE and PHP4TS.DLL to the Xitami directory and adding the
following to defaults.cfg (or whatever):

[filter]
    .php=php.exe
    .php3=php.exe
    .phtml=php.exe

This works here.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Aug  8 06:05:11 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Wed, 08 Aug 2001 00:05:11 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] URL arg problems
In-Reply-To: <3B706C42.5D5FA2C0@esite-me.net>
References: <3.0.6.32.20010726220846.007d1c20@pop.crosswinds.net>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010808000511.007af100@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 03:31 PM 8/7/01 -0700, you wrote:
>"Thomas J. Hruska" wrote:
>
>> If you want to use relative 'Location:' headers like you have above, you
>> will need to use XiFusion as Xitami (latest stable release) does not
>
>Ok, I installed XiFusion, but it still does not work. I can get
>phpinfo() to work, but if I try using an alias and "Location" or an
>alias/menu.php?menu=1&submenu=1, I get:
>Error spawning child process.
>
>Maybe I cannot use aliases??  That would really suck.  The log files are
>pretty mute on what went wrong.  Running NT SP6.

The message "Error spawning child process" occurs when PHP fails to open
the requested file.  PHP will return a non-zero return code, which causes
the error.  The log files will show nothing since XiFusion handles everything.

Aliases won't work.  That's an issue that I didn't think about during the
design of XiFusion.  XiFusion puts your CGI starting point in the webpage
root of Xitami (or whatever DOCUMENT_ROOT is set to) for security reasons.
If you have to bypass XiFusion to get to an alias, use an absolute
"off-site" Location URL:

header("Location:
http://www.mysubserver.myserver.com/alias/menu.php?menu=1&submenu=1");

OR without XiFusion:

header("Location: /alias/menu.php?menu=1&submenu=1");

Both will be passed back to the browser for processing (slower than
server-side processing, but should work).  I still recommend using XiFusion
even in your case as you will probably not hop all over the place too
often.  If you will be using Aliases more often than not, then don't use
XiFusion.

The first Location URL is viewed by XiFusion to be an "off-site" absolute
URL.  For these types of URLs, XiFusion will pass the Location back to the
server and the server will pass them back to the client to process.  The
second Location URL is viewed by XiFusion as an absolute URL on the current
server and will do server-side redirection without regard to Aliases.
Without XiFusion, the second method is passed back to the browser which
will then contact Xitami.  Remember, Xitami knows about Aliases, XiFusion
does not.  Also note that Aliases generally take more time to process.

Hope this helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Aug  8 12:51:09 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Joachim Benjamins)
Date: Wed, 08 Aug 2001 10:51:09 -0100
Subject: [Xitami] Re: default.ida?XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX
Message-ID: <20010808105349-34826-10@mailbackup.mensys.nl>

On Tue, 07 Aug 2001 20:28:39 -0700, john.uhlig@coconutcomm.com wrote:

>If there's a solution, I as well as everyone else would love to hear it. I am
>getting hit every 5-10 minutes, multiple times. There are a lot of hits from
>the 63.196.xxx.xxx class. Wish my firewall could block whole IP blocks...

You can set it up in your IP stack (at least on OS/2) by using the following trick:

Banning certain IP addesses from your server can be usefull if some client is overloading you 
with IP requests (certain web-indexers appear to behave like this - and Code Red apparently) 

You can achieve this by adding the following statement to x:\MPTN\BIN\SETUP.CMD (on an OS/2 
system!)

route add -net 209.67.229.138 -netmask 255.255.255.255 127.0.0.1 -blackhole 

This causes a request from 209.67.229.138 to be ignored by the server. Since it will not get any
response, they may want to stop attacking... 
The bad thing is that i don't think you can use wildcards so you may want to add a whole bunch 
of addresses, or scan your log and automatically add the IP address of the default.ida? 
requester.

Of course it assumes the availability of a localhost (ifconfig lo 127.0.0.1) 
It's the result of some experimenting with BSD-like commands for routing, on Warp Server for
eBusiness.

Good luck,

Joachim Benjamins.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Aug  8 22:03:01 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael)
Date: Wed, 8 Aug 2001 17:03:01 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] I wanna get this guy
In-Reply-To: <000001c1203e$10316ba0$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com>
Message-ID: <3B7170C5.28483.1ED3D3A@localhost>

If you were the world-famous author I'd say use "fuzzy logic" but you 
might be someone else.  ;D

There are far more weird people in the world then there is time to track 
them down.  If the information and images are too revealing you may 
want to tone the site down a little until the "stalker" gets bored and 
leaves.

There could be some rational and totally non-weird reason for their 
behavior you haven't thought of.   You might just have your first groupie!  

If they have a static ip you might try searches (esp google) for the ip as 
this sometimes appears in some listings.

Put in comment areas, esp in places the lurker frequents.  Gather 
information as it's amazing how far you can get on just a little 
information.  If they play an instrument, such as a cello, they are 
probably listed in a music directory somewhere.  My oldest daughter, a 
budding geneologist, can track down nearly anyone but without a huge 
budget she needs more than just an ip.

Also, change your website around.  Keep the root level clean without 
links and change the directory names for areas you'd prefer to keep 
more  private.  If the lurker quickly finds their way into the private areas, 
you know to look within close circles or co-workers.

Michael Alft
http://alft.net/software
Online Since '89

My sites are not on any search engine as they are private audience only.
Thyen a robot started indexing one area every two hours or so.  This was a
photo area with thumbnails and fullsize images meant to show a camera
manufacturer what was wrong with my new digital camera.  This  indexing
went on for days.  The only people who knew about it were the camera store
and national repair depot

The second page was a page of photos taken by us linked from our personal
page.  The only way to know it's there is to link from the main page which
I recently put into my email signature.  I made about half a dozen posts to
two mailing lists.  Then I started getting junk mail and another robot
started accessing that and another area every few hours.

In both cases of robot indexing, the answer was simple.  I just put a
webserver password in those areas and it stopped.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug  9 20:21:20 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 10 Aug 2001 07:21:20 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Sub directory access
In-Reply-To: Message from john.uhlig@coconutcomm.com
 of "Thu, 09 Aug 2001 11:05:21 MST." <997380321@coconutcomm.com>
Message-ID: <200108091921.HAA25458@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <997380321@coconutcomm.com>, john.uhlig@coconutcomm.com writes:
>Hmm, maybe that is the problem - the "index" listing of all user pages are
>created dynamically for every request, depending on the user input, i.e.
>searching a particular region. I *assumed* that if I submitted the TLD to
>search engines, that it would automatically get all subdirectories under that
>domain. So what you are saying is that there should be a hard coded index page
>with links to all of the directories/pages under the TLD?

Search engine spiders (the things that index pages) work by getting a
page (eg, the top level page) and then following the links in that, and
the links in the pages that gets to and the links in the pages that gets
to and...

If you've got a bunch of directories that _are_ links to from the index
page at the front, it'll find them fairly easily.  If you've got a bunch
of pages which aren't linked from there (and/or aren't linked from
anywhere but CGI scripts, which generally search engines will avoid
running) then it won't be able to find them, since it doesn't know to
look.

As someone else said, either rearrange your site so that there's a set
of links that leads there, or submit the URLs separately.

If a web browser can access the pages, so can an indexing spider.  The
question is "does it know that it should"?

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug  9 20:43:01 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Richard Donahue)
Date: Thu, 9 Aug 2001 14:43:01 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Sub directory access
References: <997379320@coconutcomm.com>
Message-ID: <002601c1210b$80106700$0201a8c0@midco.net>

<meta name="revisit_after" content="30 days">
<meta name="robots" content="index">

Put that on your index page. Also, it takes a while for the pages to show up
in the search engines.

-Rich

Someone was trying to use your Xitami server as a web proxy.  Either
they'd inadvertantly thought that it was, or they were just
experimenting to see what was set up insecurely.  In either case Xitami
isn't a web proxy, so it just mutters darkly about these things and
moves on.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Aug 10 08:55:49 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Fri, 10 Aug 2001 02:55:49 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] CodeRed solution...
In-Reply-To: <3B4C7748.29ED99F0@evernet.net>
References: <200107100736.TAA05304@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>
 <3B4AFCF0.2145FE19@qwest.net>
 <3B4B8055.FE5F61FB@home.com>
 <3B4C4BF1.577EAF5A@2cah.com>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010810025549.007a73f0@pop.crosswinds.net>

>From what I can tell, most people now have CodeRed II (my log files for the
past 24 hours only show CodeRed II).  So, here is what we can do to help
the poor souls out :)

Write a PHP script called default.ida.  Now, instead of replying with an
e-mail (as someone suggested), make the script take advantage of the fact
that cmd.exe is now in an executable location on the remote server (as
root.exe).  So, what the script should do is execute root.exe to launch FTP
to go and download the patch from Microsoft.  Then, use root.exe to FTP
down a macro script from your sever (to simulate keypresses).  Then run the
macro script on the remote server using root.exe one last time to execute
the macro script which will install the patch (the macro script should also
remove root.exe as well as reboot the machine when it's done).  Thus, we
can effectively remove CodeRed II on the remote server and patch IIS at the
same time...Microsoft never made fixes this simple :)


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

Have you pondered the legality of modifying someone else's computer 
without their consent?   Wouldn't you be suspect for damages, real or 
imagined?  

Some people are going to be really po'd when they discover they have to 
reformat everything on their local network.  As very few good deeds go 
unpunished, I don't think I want them looking in my direction.  

Also, I don't see that you've removed the backdoor or other backdoors 
that may have also arrived.  Would you further help these people by 
reformatting their computer remotely?  Surely you realize that hackers 
are applying their own automated routines but for other purposes?

The people to help is Microsoft.  At first I thought that everyone should 
relay all these gazillions of daily hits to them so they will learn to be 
more responsible than to default bug-ridden internet software in the next 
os.   On second thought I suspect that giant armies of slaved machines 
are probably getting ready to do just  that ~ and worse.

Michael

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Aug 10 10:55:14 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Fri, 10 Aug 2001 10:55:14 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] port fowarding and verizon
Message-ID: <43980@dsl.co.uk>

In message <3B737162.8F92ECCA@alum.rpi.edu> evan heller writes:
> Hi:
> 
> I'm not sure how many of you use verizon for dsl but recently due to 
> the code red virus, they have now filtered all port 80 requests. So, 
> does anyone know how to set up either xitami (or using zoneedit.com) 
> to redirect all port 80 requests to port say 8006?  That way my sites 
> are still available but no one will know the better? Thanks

Huh?  I fail to see what use it would be to modify anything on YOUR
machine: if Verizon are filtering port 80, then no request will get
anywhere near your machine.

You could run Xitami on a different port, but people would have to be
told to contact, say http://your.host:8006/ instead of plain
http://your.host/.

I would think that your best course of action is to show Verizon that you
don't like them interfering with YOUR traffic (on the specious grounds
that some OTHER customers may be too stupid to know that they're running
a buggy piece of MicroCrap), and move to a different ISP.  If you have a
public forum (such as a newsgroup) within the Verizon camp for other
customers, I suggest you start campaigning therein.

Oh, and while you're at it, please adjust your mailer so that it wraps
lines automatically; your post consisted of two very long lines of text
(the first was 255 characters).  The accepted norm in e-mail and usenet
is 72--76 characters per line; note that the very recently published new
standard for e-mail, RFC-2822, still insists that lines should be of this
sort of length (although permitting longer ones WHERE APPROPRIATE).

-- 
Brian {Hamilton Kelly}                                          bhk@dsl.co.uk
    "We have gone from a world of concentrated knowledge and wisdom to one of
    distributed ignorance.  And we know and understand less while being incr-
    easingly capable."              Prof. Peter Cochrane, formerly of BT Labs

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Aug 10 19:55:51 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Jim Brown)
Date: Fri, 10 Aug 2001 14:55:51 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] can't run "exec" from shtml
In-Reply-To: <000101c121c8$f3843c30$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com>
References: <000101c121c8$f3843c30$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com>
Message-ID: <3672510704.20010810145551@mediaone.net>

Hi Jill,

   Are you running any other CGI's successfully???  If not I'd check that
   you enabled the ENV variable SSI_INSECURE or config...

[Security]
    Ssi_insecure=yes

Ref: http://www.imatix.com/html/xitami/index6.htm#TOC64

> #exec cmd="command"
>    
> Executes a native command and includes the output of this command. Note that
>     the command runs in the main Xitami directory. This SSI command - which is a
>     potential security risk for your system - is only accepted if the environment
>     variable SSI_INSECURE is set to 'yes'. (Under Windows NT, in the System Control
>     Panel, under 'Environment'; under Windows 95 by adding 'SET SSI_INSECURE=yes'
>     to the autoexec.bat.)



                                         Best Regards,
                                              Jim

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Aug 10 21:13:27 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ted Heske)
Date: Fri, 10 Aug 2001 16:13:27 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Sub directory access
In-Reply-To: <3B743955.EF78EBFF@nii.net>
Message-ID: <000001c121d8$ea848350$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com>

Most of the info on this site is new to me also.  Yes, it is that simple to
run your own website with xitami.  It really does install and run with no
additional configuration.

I advise a persistent connection, like cable modem or ADSL.  In my case I
have ADSL thru mindspring.  Because my IP address is dynamic (changes all
the time) I subscribe to TZO, a dynamic DNS service, to make sure my domain
name can always be resolved with the constantly changing IP address.  I
believe Xitami may offer this service also, although I'm not sure.  Anyhoo,
once you have a simple website functioning you can begin to mire yourself in
the config and admin details.  Hope this helps.

Jill

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Richard Donahue)
Date: Fri, 10 Aug 2001 15:49:53 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Sub directory access
References: <997379320@coconutcomm.com> <002601c1210b$80106700$0201a8c0@midco.net> <3B743955.EF78EBFF@nii.net>

It's not real difficult to run your own basic Web server for serving up
pages. Xitami runs with no configuration. Be careful on what machine you run
it on though, for security reasons. TZO, will work for you if you have
dynamic IP addressing. If you have static, you could use zoneedit.com and
edit your own zone (domain). You can run you own mail server too. I use
Mercury/32, www.pmail.com .

-Rich

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 11 00:01:17 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 11 Aug 2001 11:01:17 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] xml file load error
In-Reply-To: Message from "Toernooi Assistent" <toernooi.assistent@hccnet.nl>
 of "Fri, 10 Aug 2001 21:51:15 +0200." <003701c121d5$d90d6950$9600000a@MINE1>
Message-ID: <200108102301.LAA09762@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <003701c121d5$d90d6950$9600000a@MINE1>, "Toernooi Assistent" writes:
>after upgrading Xitami from 4d7 to 5b5, loading of an host xml file by an
>html page with jscript (xmldom) stopped working. 

I take it you mean 25b5.  In 25b5 configuration, XML files are marked
for handling by the xixxml extension (which runs GSL over them).  If
you just want to serve out XML files you need to defeat this, which
currently can only be done by commenting out the [wsx] .xml=xixxml
line in _xitami.cfg_.  (You can't override it in the other config files;
there's a bug against this.)

24d9 shouldn't have this problem, as it doesn't try to handle XML files
in any particularly special manner, it just sends them out.

BTW, the debug log can be very useful for tracking this sort of thing
down. (Providing you set [server] debug=1 and try it again.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 11 00:08:08 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 11 Aug 2001 11:08:08 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Redirecting an URL to another port
In-Reply-To: Message from "Becky R. Izen - MSSP" <bizen@jfsmssp.org>
 of "Fri, 10 Aug 2001 14:58:45 MST." <3B73F6A5.12586.625216F@localhost>
Message-ID: <200108102308.LAA10045@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3B73F6A5.12586.625216F@localhost>, "Becky R. Izen - MSSP" writes:
>How would I redirect a request for a specific page (for example, 
>default.ida) to another port (such as 4080)?

Intelligent front end proxy?

Certainly for CodeRed you can't hope to send it a redirect! 

About the only other thing I could think of is that you could run a
LRWP, filter, etc, that received the request on port 80 (which is where
it WILL be made), and then made another connectin to port 4080 on your
machine, and then returned the result of that.

I can't for the life of me think of why you'd want to waste resources
doing that.

FWIW, I do know that some ISPs are using their intelligent transparent
proxies to either block the CodeRed requests, or direct them somewhere
other than their webservers.  But those things tend to be Rather
Expensive (tm).

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 11 02:38:22 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 11 Aug 2001 13:38:22 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Redirecting an URL to another port
In-Reply-To: Message from "Joe Byrne" <Joe@byrneworld.com>
 of "Fri, 10 Aug 2001 20:19:24 EST." <FNEAKJNHKIFEIAHOLMPCOEEPCDAA.Joe@ByrneWorld.com>
Message-ID: <200108110138.NAA11739@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <FNEAKJNHKIFEIAHOLMPCOEEPCDAA.Joe@ByrneWorld.com>, "Joe Byrne" writes:
>   I don't know if this is Becky's reason or not, but I too have tried to do
>this.  I have a web based email application (rather popular one by Windows
>standards) that runs on port 3001.  My clients get their mail bu going to:
>http://mail.domainname.com:3001.  Great, but most of my customer don't
>understand ports and I end up fielding a lot of calls because they get my
>home page instead of their email.  I've ended up running the email and web
>servers on two different machines to avoid the port problem, but I also have
>a calendar application that runs (by default) on port 8060.  I really don't
>want to license 3 copies of Windows (almost the cost of the hardware!) just
>to make the lives of my customers easy, but I don't have a lot of choice.

You don't need three copies of Windows.  You need 1 copy of NT Server
or 2000 (assuming that you _have_ to use Windows due to the software you
need; any modern Unix/Linux system can do this just as easily).  Then you
bind three IP addresses to the _same_ server (NT Server and 2000 can do
this; 95/98/ME, etc cannot).  Then you configure Xitami, and whatever
other programs that you want to listen on _one_ of those IP addresses
(each).  (Xitami can be configured to do this with the [server] ipaddress
setting; by default it is "*" which means "everything you can find".)

If you have only one IP address to play with (and it sounds like you
don't, if setting three machines up is a feasible option), then you need
to look at doing some sort of selective request forwarding -- ie, having
a program that handles the request, connects to the "real thing", and
then passes back the reply it gets.  With Xitami something like LRWP
would be required for this, or if you're lucky with the URLs used a
filter or CGI script.  (Filters are basically CGI, but run with the
input being the original page before filtering -- you can ignore that
and make it all up yourself if you want.)

If you don't care about all your users that are behind corporate
firewalls being blocked from accessing it, you can run your other
servers on off-numbered ports, and send redirects.  If you need to do
this only for a few basic URLs a CGI or filter would be sufficient for
this; just have it return a Location: header with the new location.
(But any user behind a corporate firewall that says port-80-outside
only, will get redirected, but otherwise not be able to access the
service.)

As I commented in my earlier message this is not a solution to the
codered type problem, as you'll just end up causing more work for your
system not less.  Only by having another machine in front (eg, a
transparent proxy or a reverse proxy) that can do that filtering off do
you save anything.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 11 05:08:04 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Jeff Hamblin)
Date: Fri, 10 Aug 2001 21:08:04 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Another CodeRed solution...
References: <3B743283.28517.AC87E8@localhost> <3B7468EF.26066.181234A@localhost>
Message-ID: <003401c1221b$3aa29740$0d00a8c0@dt1.sdca.home.com>

Code Red Vigilante:

 http://www.dynwebdev.com/codered/

Basically it listens on port 80 (nothing else can be on port 80, of course,
so it mean you can't run a web server with this too). When it detects a Code
Red connection from an infected machine, it then uses the shell access of
the infected computer to pop up a window on the infected computer's screen
saying their computer is infected and giving info on how to get rid of the
infection.

Seems more constructive than some suggestions... :)



From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 11 05:59:46 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Sat, 11 Aug 2001 00:59:46 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Sub directory access
References: <997379320@coconutcomm.com> <002601c1210b$80106700$0201a8c0@midco.net> <3B743955.EF78EBFF@nii.net>
Message-ID: <3B74BBC2.5FE8BDB7@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  I understand I can host my own web site with the xitami server and use a regular isp as a "backbone."  Is this true,

Install Xitami. 

Open a browser on the same PC and tell it to open
"http://localhost". You see Xitami's default page. You can edit
or replace that with your own page. 

Now, do you want everybody in the world to see it? To do so, they
need to know how to find your machine and they strictly need an
IP number like 257.103.87.290. However if your IP number is
listed in a DNS server (generally your ISP has one) they can type
a friendly URL instead of the IP number and the DNS will look-up
the right number for them. 

If you use a dial-up connection, you get a different IP number
every time you dial. There are ways to get this to "work", but
they are clumsy and you may not want to have the phone line open
all day and night. (Most ISPs will drop your connection if idle.)

If you use a cable-modem or DSL line, you are on-line all the
time. However your IP number *may* change from time to time, as
the ISP adjusts their routers, or frankly to make it hard to run
a server when paying for a home-only connection. 

What you really want is an always-on connection with a "fixed IP"
address, and DNS service that links a friendly URL like
"pauls-site.nii.net" to that IP number. That's usually more
expensive than a simple home-surfer connection. 

In my case, I'm in a school with decent backbone connection.
However it cost well over $5,000 to get this building connected
(not wired, just to have a router patched to the campus
backbone). That covers a couple dozen workers and 5 public
webservers, but was still quite a gulp. 

 -PRR

I'm pretty sure only NT and 2000, running an unpatched IIS, are vulnerable
to Code Red.

During the first few days of the CRII onslaught, I'd take a few minutes a
day and plug the IP addresses of infected machines (gleaned from my xitami
error logs) into my web browser. If a website loaded, and there were any
contact email addresses available, I sent them a note about their 'problem.'
I actually got a few thank you's. The 'fun' wore off rather quickly. The
Code Red Vigilante approach is much more efficient.

Something interesting to note is a debate currently on the @home tech
support newsgroups. As many know, the terms of service for @home 'forbid'
users operating web servers. What's interesting is that the @home user
webpages support MS Frontpage extensions, and @home recommends that users
use Frontpage 2000 to create and maintain their @home website. Installing
Frontpage 2000 installs IIS on the local machine to host the local copy of
the website (for previewing I presume). Many users don't realize they have a
web server running!! They're just following the recommendation of their ISP!

I know this is a bit off-topic. But everybody seems to be tired of their
logs filling up. I'm still getting about 20 CRII hits an hour. I'm not so
much concerned about that in itself. I'm concerned about what's going to
happen when all these infected machines that have a wide-open backdoor start
getting exploited.

What I am REALLY concerned about is ISPs using this as an excuse to block
port 80. AT&T has already done it. I expect more will follow suit.

-Jeff H

Only Windows NT/2000 machines running IIS 4/5 are vulnerable to the attack.

Don't wait for your ISP to start blocking ports. Write to them now telling
them that you do NOT run a web server that can be exploited by Code Red. Tell
them that if they block HTTP requests that you will find another ISP who is
more attuned to the real world.

movement". Don't let your ISP determine what gets to your server, it is not
their place. This is an administrative issue, not an ISP issue. Take the
initiative. Hit them where it hurts, paying the bill.

It is just like voting in the states, the powers that be are there to serve

From: "Ewen McNeill" <ewen@imatix.com>

> In message <003701c121d5$d90d6950$9600000a@MINE1>, "Toernooi Assistent"
writes:
> >after upgrading Xitami from 4d7 to 5b5, loading of an host xml file by an
> >html page with jscript (xmldom) stopped working.
>
> I take it you mean 25b5.  In 25b5 configuration, XML files are marked
> for handling by the xixxml extension (which runs GSL over them).  If
> you just want to serve out XML files you need to defeat this, which
> currently can only be done by commenting out the [wsx] .xml=xixxml
> line in _xitami.cfg_.  (You can't override it in the other config files;
> there's a bug against this.)
>
> 24d9 shouldn't have this problem, as it doesn't try to handle XML files
> in any particularly special manner, it just sends them out.
>
> BTW, the debug log can be very useful for tracking this sort of thing
> down. (Providing you set [server] debug=1 and try it again.)
>
> Ewen

Yes, but not if you call all the files ".xml".  You'll have to use one

On 9 Aug 2001, at 19:37, Ted Heske wrote:

> Michael,
> 
> Thanks very much for the reference to your SSI script.  I will try it.  I am
> a *complete* newbie so I'm sure it will take me a while to get it working.
> I wondered if you could clarify some of the tips you gave me earlier:
> 
> > Keep the root level clean without
> > links and change the directory names for areas you'd prefer to keep
> > more  private.
> 
> I'm not sure what you mean by "keep the root level clean without links."
> Also, how do I keep areas more private by changing directory names?  Can't
> people just view the HTML source and get whatever directory info they want.
> Remember, I'm a bigtime newbie.  This is my first website and I know zip
> about security.  Thanks very much again, and by the way, keep an eye out for
> our new book, scheduled to come out next year.
> 
> Jill



Be sure to add me to your email list when your book comes out.

You shouldn't start out trying to get web site security by using methods 
like robots.txt, logins and passwords, scripting, filtering, etc.

Keeping the root level clean and without links simply means don't do what 
most people do which is link to everything in the web site.  Lurkers can find 
anything and search engines will rip your entire site in seconds and put it 
on public display.

Consider your root level the base of the tree.  Lurkers and others come in 
but that's all they see.  A dead end :::gasp:::

Now you can list subdirectories or branches with search engines.  The very 
most a lurker or search engine can get is that branch.  Everything else is 
invivisible unless they know it exists.  For instance, on the same domain, 
clients can get business stuff but only special people can see pictures of 
me and the family getting sunburned at Disneyworld this summer.

If a lurker finds their way into places you'd rather they didn't, all you need 
to do is change the directory name and *poof* it's invisible again and 
there's no need to redo all your links or redo logins and passwords.  You 
will have to contact those who you wish to see certain pages.  
Surprisingly, the list of people who are able to see me with Mickey Mouse 
is quite small. (Hi Mom!)

Xitami is a great web server for the home but people with one computer 
:::gasp again::: who share their most personal stuff on the same box as 
their web pages are nuts.  Xitami don't require much firepower so if you 
want lots of instant security, dedicate a cheap $200 computer for your web 
server.

Have fun!

Michael

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Aug 12 01:21:50 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Sat, 11 Aug 2001 20:21:50 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] RE: Bigtime Newbie
References: <000001c1226c$9e79cf80$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com>
Message-ID: <3B75CC1E.2A0846AD@rci.rutgers.edu>

> After zillions of these probes I do not find root.exe anywhere on any of my systems.  

Good. You should NOT have root.exe. It is really CMD (NT's
improved COMMAND.COM) moved by the virus to where a hacker can
access it. 

> Is there some reason to believe that Code Red can infiltrate my system even thru Xitami?

CodeRed targets a very specific set of bugs in MS IIS server and
the indexing service that goes with NT. If you send a very large
request to IIS, it will over-write memory that isn't supposed to
be used to store the request ("buffer overrun"). Apparently the
memory it overwrites is program code that can be subverted by
overwriting it with the hacker's code. Now the hacker has a way
to run software on the victim machine. 

Xitami appears to not have the buffer overrun problem (maybe
because it was written by smart suspicious people instead of the
kids at Microsoft). And even if it did, the memory "beyond" the
buffer is not the susceptible code found in IIS Indexing. Even if
it were program code, it would not be the same code as IIS, so a
bug written for IIS would not infect, just die.

If you wonder if you may be susceptible (it is possible to have
IIS running without knowing it) go to eEye's site
http://www.eeye.com/html/Research/Tools/codered.html and download
the scanner. You need to know your IP number; you can scan up to
255 IP numbers in one pass. A tip: use the "Show All Servers"
option so you know what non-IIS servers are on your network. I
found a PWS server downstairs that the owner didn't know about.
PWS is a cut-down IIS, but apparently not vulnerable. 

 -PRR

>java.lang.AbstractMethodError 

Either (a) you're using the wrong version of the JSDK (servlet API) when
you compiled your servlet, or (b) you're using the wrong version of the
JSDK when you're running your servlet.  Hence the methods
provided/required don't match, hence the error you get.

The iMatix Servlet Runner uses a fairly old JSDK (1.0 or 1.1, I forget)
and won't work with the newer ones without changes because, as usual
with Java programs, the interface keeps changing all the time.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Aug 12 14:01:26 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Owen Rudge)
Date: Sun, 12 Aug 2001 14:01:26 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Can't get PHP to run (despite reading Xitami-FAQ)
References: <1383926370.20010812144608@gmx.net>
Message-ID: <006a01c1232e$e653bd80$4d98fc3e@rudge>

I've answered this question many times recently. I think it should be put in
the FAQ.

Try copying PHP.EXE and PHP4TS.DLL to the Xitami directory and adding the
following to defaults.cfg (or whatever):

[filter]
    .php=php.exe
    .php3=php.exe
    .phtml=php.exe

This works here.

Owen Rudge
http://www.owenrudge.co.uk/
http://www.gamearchive.uk.tt/

overload then it crashes and requires you to restart.

a flock error or some other internal error, so check
your interpretor (#!user/blah/blah)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Aug 12 21:42:29 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Sun, 12 Aug 2001 16:42:29 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] 2 questions
References: <3B769A11.464D7404@nii.net>
Message-ID: <3B76EA35.DBD17998@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  I forgot my user name and password 

The superuser password is in plain-text in the file xitami.aut	

> my scripts which use input from user forms.  I tried putting in a long string of characters (like 300) to see if the text would wrap and they didn't.  

Wrap in the final output or wrap in the HTML Form? 

If you want to see it wrapped in the browser as the user is
inputting, Perl can't help because the text does not get to perl
until the user hits Submit. You may be wanting text wrap in the
browser. 

There is a WRAP=Off|Soft|Hard parameter for the textarea tag that
specifies wrapping for the form-user's convenience. It works
differently in different browsers and is generally pretty crude. 

 {textarea NAME="foo" ROWS="3" COLS="40" wrap=Hard}

See for example: 

http://www.blooberry.com/indexdot/html/tagpages/t/textarea.htm

 -PRR

Morning.

A 2 part challenge.  This CGI is running on a Win32 platform, but I would like the solution to work on any.  I've got a few hours of Googling on this but don't seem to be hitting the right keyword combos, and I couldn't find anything helpful in the local bookstore computer section.  I've read through the O'reilly DBI, CGI.pm, Programming Perl and Perl Cookbook manuals and the cpan.org security mods section but haven't found what I'm looking for.

First part.  I have been searching for a simple way to password protect a Perl CGI program.  (I'm using CGI.pm and DBI.pm).  I don't need heavy authentication, just basic security - something to keep casual browsers out.  Is there a Perl module that can supply this functionality?  If so, is there a HOWTO?  If not, has anyone written a secure front-end (Perl or HTML/CGI.pm) to a Perl CGI that they are willing to share?  I can see how to do it without a libmod, but I think I'd just be re-inventing, and probably not as well as someone who does this all the time.

Second part.  At this time, a user can bookmark this CGI location, bypassing any password protection scheme.  Is there some way around this using Perl and/or HTML?  I've seen this with forms using ASP or PHP but haven't found it with Perl.  It seems to me that the CGI is static, and I can't think of a way to keep it from being loaded if someone goes directly to the page, unless the password code is an integral part of the code itself - but this becomes a hassle for folks who are doing multiple entries (20 -30) at one session.

All helpful thoughts accepted.  I will compile and post the results to ADV-HTML, including replies from other lists referenced.

Aloha!

David

Technology Development Office, College of Education, USC

Hi david
if you dont get anyone else replying to your perl questions drop me a line
at garry@cable.net.nz

i have written basic security scripts and can easily deal with those
bookmarking the page that is secured.
you simply make the page part of a script and do.....  if
($ENV{'HTTP_REFERER'} ne "$myip") {print
"location:path/to/login/script.pl\n\n";} before your page is displayed by
the script.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Aug 13 19:30:47 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael)
Date: Mon, 13 Aug 2001 14:30:47 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Password protected Perl CGI.
In-Reply-To: <sb77bf12.020@GWM.SC.EDU>
Message-ID: <3B77E497.17890.160B5C4@localhost>


If all you want to do is keep the contents of a text script private, why not 
use a simple script to call the actual working script which is kept in a 
different location not visible to the internet?   You can point to scripts and 
pass variables anywhere ~ to other local drives or other machines.  You 
and your scripts have complete access.  To the internet user only the 
calling script is visible.

You could also cripple the working script so that it only responds to local 
calls from your machine and bails out if not.

If working remotely you can pass a field variable to the machine so it 
recognizes you.

Not sure about your multiplatform and privacy needs but you should 
consider using programming software with compilers.

Michael

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Aug 14 01:54:34 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Mon, 13 Aug 2001 19:54:34 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Password protected Perl CGI.
In-Reply-To: <sb77bf12.020@GWM.SC.EDU>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010813195434.007c7650@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 11:50 AM 8/13/01 -0400, David Michaels writeth:
>
>First part.  I have been searching for a simple way to password protect a
Perl CGI program.  (I'm using CGI.pm and DBI.pm).  I don't need heavy
authentication, just basic security - something to keep casual browsers
out.  Is there a Perl module that can supply this functionality?  If so, is
there a HOWTO?  If not, has anyone written a secure front-end (Perl or
HTML/CGI.pm) to a Perl CGI that they are willing to share?  I can see how
to do it without a libmod, but I think I'd just be re-inventing, and
probably not as well as someone who does this all the time.

Have you tried putting the CGI in its own directory and then modified your
Xitami configuration to password protect the directory?  This usually stops
most people from attempting to get it.  If someone tries to get it by brute
force or it is obvious in the logs that someone is doing something that you
don't want them to do, you can block the IP.

>Second part.  At this time, a user can bookmark this CGI location,
bypassing any password protection scheme.  Is there some way around this
using Perl and/or HTML?  I've seen this with forms using ASP or PHP but
haven't found it with Perl.  It seems to me that the CGI is static, and I
can't think of a way to keep it from being loaded if someone goes directly
to the page, unless the password code is an integral part of the code
itself - but this becomes a hassle for folks who are doing multiple entries
(20 -30) at one session.

Do some type of session-management-thingy...that way you can force people
to log in/enter a password to get into the system between browser
sessions/time limits (there are two types of sessions, sessions that
persist until the browser closes, and sessions that persist until time runs
out - some websites use both methods).

Hope this helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Aug 14 09:54:24 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 14 Aug 2001 20:54:24 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] upload
In-Reply-To: Message from Andreas Zieritz <zieritz@sovik.no>
 of "Tue, 14 Aug 2001 09:52:14 +0200." <3B78D8AE.5A458481@sovik.no>
Message-ID: <200108140854.UAA23162@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3B78D8AE.5A458481@sovik.no>, Andreas Zieritz writes:
>My specific problem is that, after compiling the program and copying the
>configuration file to the /cgi-bin directory I am constantly getting a
>'I could not open the configuration file' error. The upload.cfg has
>664-rights in the /cgi-bin directory.

Your CGI script and Xitami differ as to their idea of what the current
directory should be when the cgi script is run, and your CGI script is
using a relative path.  

By default Xitami sets the current directory to the CGI directory when
running CGI scripts; but it seems that your CGI script expects something
else.

You can either change your CGI script to have a full path, or change its
assumption about what the current directory will be, or change what
Xitami sets the current directory to when running CGI scripts ([CGI]
workdir).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

In message <001301c11fb8$e9923040$0201a8c0@midco.net>, "Richard Donahue" writes:
>server. My Webmask is set to:
>Webmask=!63.6.*,*
>Is that the correct pattern to exclude the 63.6.* addresses from the server?

Yes, that's the right syntax.  But make sure you're setting the right
webmask!  (There are three of them in the config file :-) )  The one you
want is [security] webmask.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Aug 14 09:58:50 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 14 Aug 2001 20:58:50 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Password protected Perl CGI.
In-Reply-To: Message from "David Michaels" <MICHAELS@gwm.sc.edu>
 of "Mon, 13 Aug 2001 11:50:30 -0400." <sb77bf12.020@GWM.SC.EDU>
Message-ID: <200108140858.UAA23282@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <sb77bf12.020@GWM.SC.EDU>, "David Michaels" writes:
>First part.  I have been searching for a simple way to password protect a Perl 
>CGI program.  

1. Let the webserver do it with basic authentication. 

2. Have the CGI pretend to do basic authentication, by sending
   authentication required responses out unless it sees the right
   authentication header.  (Basic authentication is just that, basic.
   I've done it in a few lines of code several times, and if you can
   live with a hard coded username/password it's even easier.)

Basic authentication is robust against someone book marking the page;
they'll be prompted once-per-session when they come back to the page.

Xitami can do all of this for you if you set up the xitami.aut file
appropriately.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Aug 14 10:23:13 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 14 Aug 2001 21:23:13 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] supervisor agent and logs
In-Reply-To: Message from "Michael S. Kazarin" <kazarin@eltra.metrocom.ru>
 of "Tue, 07 Aug 2001 11:30:47 +0400." <00fc01c11f12$e45bac10$659305c3@futeltra>
Message-ID: <200108140923.VAA24031@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <00fc01c11f12$e45bac10$659305c3@futeltra>, "Michael S. Kazarin" writes:
>Ewen wrote:
>| You might be better working with it, to tell it not to remove log files
>| as often.  You can configure the log rotation and how long they're kept
>| in the Xitami configuration file as well.
>
>How do I actually do that? I have my logs cycled daily, so there is a file
>for each day.  But how can I tell it to keep more than 14 of them, 
>i. e. more than two weeks of logs.

I've just stared at the source a little, and it seems that you can't
control what the supervisor does -- it seems to have the
two-weeks-is-plenty setting hard coded into it :-(

In which case, at present, you'll either have to disable the supervisor,
or you'll have to change the source.

According to the source the Xitami supervisor can be disabled by
setting:

[server] supervisor=0

(which appears to be the default setting, in at least some versions of
Xitami.)

If it isn't the default in your version, you should set it in
defaults.cfg; that's the only place it'll be noticed, as it's checked as
xitami is starting up.  (If that doesn't work try changing xitami.cfg as
well, but I suspect that won't make a difference.)

Sorry for the confusion -- you were on the right track after all.  It
_should_ be possible to configure how long the supervisor keeps things
around though.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Aug 14 21:03:15 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Dan Orzechowski)
Date: Tue, 14 Aug 2001 16:03:15 -0400 (EDT)
Subject: [Xitami] '&' character in <textarea...> problem
In-Reply-To: <4C99842BC5F6D411A6A000805FBBB19948CB6C@ge0057exch01.agere.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.SOL.4.21.0108141556010.28321-100000@acmex.gatech.edu>

> <form action="../myscript.py" method=get>

Unless I'm mistaken, the GET method appends the form data to the URL:

http://mysite.com/myscript.py?var1=3&var2=foobar

The & symbol is used to seperate variable name/value pairs, so could it be
that when the form input is parsed, the ampersand is (incorrectly, in this
case) used as a delimiter?  I'm pretty sure this would cause the
problem you're experiencing.  Would using POST instead of GET as the form
method make a difference?  Hope this points you in the right direction.

-Dan Orzechowski
xbonesgt@cc.gatech.edu
http://xbones.resnet.gatech.edu

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Aug 15 18:16:05 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Wed, 15 Aug 2001 13:16:05 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] '&' character in <textarea...> problem
References: <4C99842BC5F6D411A6A000805FBBB19948CB69@ge0057exch01.agere.com>
Message-ID: <3B7AAE55.656D7EA2@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Python cgi module and the IE5.
> if I submit a text that contains somewhere the character
> '&', it will cut off this character and all text that follows.

Your browser may be hiding anything after a "&". Check in View Source.
NetScape seems to be smart about "&" appearing bare with no terminating
";" in sight, but other browsers may swallow everything between "&" and
the next ";" (or the end of the file!). 

I don't work with Python.

In Perl, I do this: "use CGI qw(:standard escapeHTML);"

The "CGI::escapeHTML" functions serve to escape any HTML-like markup in
the form return. "&" is the HTML prefix for non-ASCII character
entities, and for GET delimiting, so if it isn't being used as HTML it
has to be escaped. 

Python must have such a thing, and I'd look in their CGI collection
first.

 -PRR

At 20:26 2001-08-15 +0200, Toernooi Assistent wrote:
>Would there be a way to hide *.js subroutines from simple browsing?

Nope. You can't. Not easily anyway. You could use some encryption routine=20
(such as those used by most VBScript virus creators) to obfuscate your=20
scripts and then a different routine to unobf=FAscate the code, once someone=
=20
calls a  function in your script.

But, hey; You'll loose some of the original ideas about web publishing, and=
=20
no matter how well you try to obfuscate JavaScript, there'll always be=20
people who would be able to unobfuscate your obfucated code, because you=20
have to provide the unobfuscation mechanism somewhere...

If you want to make it truly hard for someone to grab your code, use server=
=20
side scripts. Preferably (if it should be beyond most code snatchers=20
knowledge) compiled ones...

/Samuel

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug 16 11:55:32 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael S. Kazarin)
Date: Thu, 16 Aug 2001 14:55:32 +0400
Subject: [Xitami] Custom Error 404 pages directories
References: <997904333@coconutcomm.com>
Message-ID: <02b601c12642$00512720$659305c3@futeltra>

I have the following set up for my server:
xitami.cfg -> [Server] -> error-script=./templates/errmain.gsl (for main
server, you might be using defaults.cfg as recommended by Imatix people)
vhost01.cfg -> [Server] -> error-script=./templates/errvhost01.gsl (for
virtual host 1)
vhost02.cfg -> [Server] -> error-script=./templates/errvhost02.gsl (for
virtual host 2)
vhost03.cfg -> [Server] -> error-script=./templates/errvhost03.gsl (for
virtual host 3)
... etc.
You have to also specify in configs the use of error-schemas: [Server] ->
use-error-script=1
In this case templates directory should be under Xitami executable directory
(in your case //xitami).

| IS there a way to specify a separate errors pages for virtual domains?
| I am hosting s few virtual domains under a directory structure as such:
|
| //xitami/webpages  (main)
| //xitami/webpages/domain1
| //xitami/webpages/domain2
| //xitami/webpages/domain3
| etc.
|
| The way it is set up (or not set up) now, every virtual domain calls the
error
| pages from the main domain. How do I change this?
| Examples of config files and directory structure would be helpful.
|
| Thanks all!

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug 16 20:39:50 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 16 Aug 2001 15:39:50 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Console.log msgs
References: <000001c12684$f41aa510$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com>
Message-ID: <3B7C2186.7E8CCB07@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Connect to : 207.69.188.186 () port 53
> Request ip address 192.168.0.2

This is an ordinary DNS look-up. The 207.69.188.186 address is similar
to the one you used to mail your note, so I assume it is your ISP's DNS
server. Port 53 is in fact DNS service (I had to check). Xitami seems to
want to know who 192.168.0.2 is. 

I'm not sure I understand the answer it gets, and I'm not sure Xitami
liked it. The "packet size error" is also odd. 

> start of authority       blackhole.isi.edu 

FWIW: http://www.isi.edu/ is the engineering school at The University of
Southern California. They say they've been around since the 1870s, and
have had a quarter million students. So the organization is legit, but
who knows what those engineering students are doing. The odd DNS results
may just mean that someone plugged in a laptop in the Lab. 

Why is Xitami doing DNS look-ups? There IS an option to do that, but we
generally leave it turned off because it is very slow. Maybe you enabled
it? 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug 16 22:56:21 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 16 Aug 2001 17:56:21 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Console.log msgs
References: <000201c12695$18e02590$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com>
Message-ID: <3B7C4185.99E31D4F@rci.rutgers.edu>

> who 192.168.0.2 is. ... That is an internal LAN address of the machine
that xitami is running on.

Duh! That's right, that range is often used for internal private IP
numbers, normally won't pass through routers, and certainly won't pass
from USC to you (unless you are on the USC campus). So the apparent
connection to USC is bogus. (I wonder how much excess load their DNS
server gets for overlapping a private range.)

Is it likely that your machine 192.168.0.2 accessed your Xitami server?
If so, and if RDNS has gotten enabled, all is OK. The bogus attempt to
ask USC for DNS look-up on your private-range IP number is awkward, but
I'm sure they are used to it. (Maybe that's why "packet size error":
maybe when their machine sees a bogus private-IP look-up, they drop the
connection ASAP.) You could run your own inside DNS server that handled
inside queries in the 192.168.0.XXX range and passed others to an
outside DNS server, but that's a lot of work just to avoid entries in
the console log. 

> Does this mean they are looking me up?  

No, that would be logged in your DNS server's logs. And it sounds like
you don't run your own DNS.

Anyway, since it is appearing in Xitami's console, it means Xitami is
looking-up 192.168.0.2. Which probably means you have RDNS enabled. 

If you basically don't want RDNS (you normally don't): In the web-admin
screen, Logging, just above "Debug reverse DNS queries",  look at
"Translate IP addresses?". You probably want this NOT checked. Below
that, "DNS servers - primary[secondary]:" you probably do NOT want this
to be a real DNS server (the default 127.0.0.1 is bogus and should foil 
all RDNS). 

 -PRR

Also, you can do this:

<script language=3D"JavaScript" type=3D"text/javascript">
<!-- Hide script from older browsers

// end hiding contents -->
</script>

or, for PDA/Phone browsing:

<SMALLSCREENIGNORE></SMALLSCREENIGNORE>

As for people hacking your code, server-side helps, but if they want it
they will get it.  You'll just have to be creative and consider the hacking
flattery, because your code is so desirable.


Cheers,

WRPalaia

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Aug 17 00:10:54 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Fri, 17 Aug 2001 00:10:54 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Console.log msgs
Message-ID: <44228@dsl.co.uk>

In message <3B7C4185.99E31D4F@rci.rutgers.edu> Paul Reid writes:
> > who 192.168.0.2 is. ... That is an internal LAN address of the machine
> that xitami is running on.
> 
> Duh! That's right, that range is often used for internal private IP
> numbers, normally won't pass through routers, and certainly won't pass
> from USC to you (unless you are on the USC campus). So the apparent
> connection to USC is bogus. (I wonder how much excess load their DNS
> server gets for overlapping a private range.)

Duh, indeed!  192.168/16 is one of the ranges allocated under RFC-1918
for "private use", and should be NATted before "meeting the Internet".
However, knowing that there has to be SOME authority for any IP address,
these are registered (see whois.arin.net) with that blackhole address in
their SOA.

However, the fact that Xitami might apparently be performing rDNS
lookups, and moreover logging them in that strange format, is less
readily explained.

    easingly capable."              Prof. Peter Cochrane, formerly of BT Labs
