From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Aug 17 23:23:32 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 18 Aug 2001 10:23:32 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] localhost problems..
In-Reply-To: Message from Dan Fisher <djf@esite-me.net>
 of "Fri, 17 Aug 2001 12:41:38 MST." <3B7D7372.1062E0D7@esite-me.net>
Message-ID: <200108172223.KAA19095@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3B7D7372.1062E0D7@esite-me.net>, Dan Fisher writes:
>So if I try http://localhost/FisherWeb/, it does not like my index.htm file:
><HTML>
><HEAD></HEAD>
><BODY BGCOLOR="#FFFFFF">
><? php header("Location:
>http://localhost/FisherWeb/menu.php?menu=1&submenu=0"); ?>
></BODY>
></HTML>

I'm not absolutely certain with PHP, but I think that it's getting
rather late to be thinking about outputting HTTP headers whenyou've
already output half of the HTML!  (For it to work, PHP would have to
scan the whole page and process the header directives first, before
outputting any of the page.)

Try turning on CGI debugging ([CGI] debug=1), and then look at the
temporary file output by accessing that page via the PHP filter.  Unless
the Location: line appears at the top of the file (in the headers
section), it won't work.

>or my index.php file:
><?  header("Location: menu.php?menu=1&submenu=0"); ?>
>
>But if I enter http://localhost/FisherWeb/menu.php?menu=1&submenu=0
>directly, it works.

This won't work because you're trying to use a relative URL for your
Location: header, and Xitami doesn't support that.  You should either
use a full "http://.../..." URL for a client side redirect, or a full path
reference "/FisherWeb/menu.php?...." for a server side redirect.

>Also, I have noticed lately that when I make a change to Xitami,
>terminate and attempt to restart, it complains that the port is already
>in use.  I have to reboot the machine to get to work again.

You _probably_ won't have to reboot the machine providing whatever is
using the port is stopped correctly.  But if you interupt a connection
which Xitami thinks is open, then you may have to wait for the "closing
connections" phase before you can restart it.

Try:

netstat -nr

from a command shell, and look to see if there are any lines for port
80 (http), particularly any that mention being in a CLOSE phase (or even
"listening").

Typical timeouts is about 5 minutes or so.  Xitami tries to tell the
operating system not to wait in this instance, but it may not get it
right for every operating system.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Aug 17 23:46:12 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Kartic Krishnamurthy)
Date: Fri, 17 Aug 2001 18:46:12 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] localhost problems..
References: <200108172223.KAA19095@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <01da01c1276e$6e316020$0245a8c0@private.solutionsforyou.com>

Hi,

I joined the list a few minutes ago and I don't know the entire background
of your problem.  However, from the PHP script you've shown, it seems that
you are outputting HTTP headers rather late in your script.

If you want to output HTTP headers, they *must* be output before any other
kind of output is sent to the browser, including HTML tags and specifically
HTML <head> tag.  Your script should actually read:
<?php
header("Location:http://.../");
?>
<HTML>
...
</HTML>

(the rest of the HTML stuff is redundant as your page will have been
redirected)  For more information on usage of header() PHP function and
associated caveats, please refer http://php.net/header

Of course, what Ewen says about either specifying http://../ or the page
relative to the webroot (/menu.php) is correct, for the Location header to
work.

Thank you,
--Kartic

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 18 02:02:59 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 18 Aug 2001 13:02:59 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Console.log msgs
In-Reply-To: Message from "Jill Heske" <jheske@atl.mindspring.com>
 of "Thu, 16 Aug 2001 14:55:01 -0400." <000001c12684$f41aa510$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com>
Message-ID: <200108180102.NAA20783@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <000001c12684$f41aa510$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com>, "Jil
l Heske" writes:
>I've got a bunch of blocks of data in my console.log file like the one
>below.  I haven't changed my xitami settings lately but this is the first I
>see of anything like this.  

The messages that you're getting seem to be from the Xitami 2.5b reverse
DNS support (to try to figure out the names of the places people are
connecting from and put them in the log file).  Given the length of the
messages they also seem to be some sort of debug messages.

Have you perhaps enabled reverse DNS recently?  And/or debugging options?

The other curious thing about the address being looked up is that it is
a "private" network address (RFC1918) which shouldn't be used on the
Internet directly.  If you are using those addresses locally you should
set up local nameserver records for 168.192.in-addr.arpa (or at least
the sections you are using).

If you are not using them locally and they are coming from the Internet,
I strongly suggest you configure your firewall to block traffic from the
Internet that uses those addresses.  They're not supposed to be used on
the Internet, but there is a lot of misconfigured networking equipment
around.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 18 02:09:33 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 18 Aug 2001 13:09:33 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] xitami aborts
In-Reply-To: Message from "Bowden, Russell" <Russell.Bowden@fiserv.com>
 of "Thu, 16 Aug 2001 17:13:22 EST." <EX-20010816-171855-0001@exchange.fiserv-missive1.fiserv.net>
Message-ID: <200108180109.NAA20890@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <EX-20010816-171855-0001@exchange.fiserv-missive1.fiserv.net>, "Bowde
n, Russell" writes:
>This is my first posting here.  I've been running Xitami with LRWP for about 2 
>years on a private network doing transaction processing on Unixware 7.1, 
>currently averaging about 4000 transactions per hour.  My problem is that 
>the Xitami process just disappears now and then.  

:-(

These sorts of problems are generally caused by a bug in the software
(ie, Xitami), where it doesn't handle something properly and either
crashes on the spot, or messes something else up causing a crash later.

I see you are running Xitami 2.5b4 -- this is a beta test version.  It's
still in beta testing because of issues like this (and because no one
has had time to go through and make it properly robust).  While there is
a 2.5b5 out, the changes between 2.5b4 and 2.5b5 are Windows-related
(for the device name denial-of-service security issue), so are unlikely
to make much difference for you.

>Sometimes (but not always) Xitami leaves behind a memtrace.lst.  
>Here's the front of one of them:

memtrace.lst is Xitami's list of memory that it knows that it's
allocated, but doesn't have any record of cleaning up properly.
Generally this means that it's exited improperly (without going through
the full close down cycle), but you know that already :-)

If your application will work with Xitam 2.4d9 (the current stable
release) you might want to consider using that.  It's known to be more
stable than the beta test version, and possibly it might avoid your
problem too.

You might also want to check the console logs (Xitami, and where ever
you directed stdout/stderr of the Xitami software) to see if there are
any further details on why it chose to exit.  Typically if it encounters
an internal error it does indicate waht it was doing at the time.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 18 02:18:26 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 18 Aug 2001 13:18:26 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Console.log msgs
In-Reply-To: Message from "Ted Heske" <theske@atl.mindspring.com>
 of "Thu, 16 Aug 2001 19:50:30 -0400." <000201c126ae$3b7a99a0$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com>
Message-ID: <200108180118.NAA21026@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <000201c126ae$3b7a99a0$0300a8c0@cashmachine.atl.mindspring.com>, "Ted Heske" writes:
>> Is it likely that your machine 192.168.0.2 accessed your Xitami server?
>
>I do access the server from its host machine, but for maintenance only (I
>log into the web admin tool).  I test my website by accessing from a
>different machine with a different IP address.  I looked up www.isi.edu and
>their IP address is nothing like 192.x.x.x (it's 128.x.x.x).  

192.168.xx.xx is an address range reserved for private internal networks.  
As a public service isi.edu (and ep.net, it seems) offer a
DNS-of-last-resort for 192.168.xx.xx to help avoid long timeouts for
people who are using those addresses internally, but haven't configured
their network properly:

bash-2.05$  nslookup -type=NS 168.192.in-addr.arpa
Server:  localhost.panix.com
Address:  127.0.0.1

Non-authoritative answer:
168.192.in-addr.arpa    nameserver = BLACKHOLE.EP.NET
168.192.in-addr.arpa    nameserver = BLACKHOLE.ISI.EDU

Authoritative answers can be found from:
BLACKHOLE.EP.NET        internet address = 198.32.1.116
BLACKHOLE.ISI.EDU       internet address = 128.9.64.26

If you are using RFC1918 addresses internally you should at least put
these addresses into the hosts file on each machine, and preferably you
should provide your own authoritive records to your local DNS server for
the RFC1918 addresses you are using, so that the "default" ones provided
as a public service by isi.edu and ep.net aren't touched.

>When does the RDNS feature actually try to translate addresses?  I see no 
>evidence that it has looked up any other addresses in the past and my 
>server gets accessed all the time.

If you have enabled RDNS translation, Xitami will try to look up the IP
addresses of machines that connect to your webserver before it writes
out the log entries.  Generally this will work, and the entries will be
logged after a short delay.

In this instance because you're using RFC1918 addresses without setting
up proper DNS records, and for some reason Xitami has taken a disliking
to the "default" ones (perhaps because they weren't what it expected to
hear back), you're getting error messages logged because Xitami is
having problems dealing with those ones.

Either set up the correct DNS records locally, or turn off RDNS in
Xitami (and, eg, resovle the addresses later, or not at all), or ignore
the messages for now.

>I do get lots of script errors while using the web admin tool so maybe 
>I shouldn't be using this version.   

What webbrowser are you using?  The webadmin portion was last updated
quite a while ago, and it's possible that it is not quite compatible
with the Javascript expected by some newer browsers.  You can turn the
Javascript off in the web based admin, and it'll basically work without
it, although occassionally you have to click on more "go" like buttons.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 18 02:21:07 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 18 Aug 2001 13:21:07 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] hiding *.js code
In-Reply-To: Message from "Toernooi Assistent" <toernooi.assistent@hccnet.nl>
 of "Wed, 15 Aug 2001 20:26:27 +0200." <002401c125b7$d2d7b780$9600000a@MINE1>
Message-ID: <200108180121.NAA21188@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <002401c125b7$d2d7b780$9600000a@MINE1>, "Toernooi Assistent" writes:
>Would there be a way to hide *.js subroutines from simple browsing?
>Scenario: client with Html pages with Javascript
>Html page needs *.js from the server.
>I am only looking for a simple hiding mechanism.

The "simple" hiding mechanism would be to use the Referer: field to
check that the right page referred to the javascript.  You'd need some
sort of CGI/filter/LRWP to serve out the Javascript after checking for
HTTP_REFERER, and to set the path for the javascript appropriately.

This will cause some problems (some things don't send the Referer field,
either deliberately or because they don't know about it), and it's
pretty easy to get around (anyone can write a program that sends
whatever it likes in the Referer field), but it'd cover your "simple
hiding mechanism" case.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 18 11:53:55 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Sat, 18 Aug 2001 11:53:55 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] localhost problems..
Message-ID: <44268@dsl.co.uk>

In message <3B7D7C2E.1C73002D@rci.rutgers.edu> Paul Reid writes:

> And what is all this "\\"? Use "/". I know DOS says "\", and c uses "\"
> as a metacharacter so you get "\\", but Xitami will translate "/" to the
> necessary path separator. And BTW, recent Windows accept "/" internally. 

It's not just "recent Windows"; internally (e.g. in functions to
open/close/delete files within a programming language, such as C, or a
scripting language, such as Rexx) one can use the forward slash as a path
separator.  I have done this in programs which have run under OS/2,
Windows 3.1, DOS (right back to v3.0), etc.

It is only if one must generate a command-line and pass it to a CLI, that
one requires backslashes.  If I find myself needing that in a program, I
have to remember to pass the '/' through a translate routine to '\'.

--

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 18 22:48:26 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Sat, 18 Aug 2001 16:48:26 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Not seeing FORM POST fields
In-Reply-To: <149418239252.20010819071720@getsoft.com>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010818164826.007b1900@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 07:17 AM 8/19/01 +1000, Neville Franks writeth:
>I've installed Xitami and PHP4 on a Windows 2000 box and everything is
>working fine except I can't see an FORM POST fields in the PHP script.
>ie. When Submit is pressed the field values are all empty when the PHP
>script processes it.

I never liked this about PHP (or at least I could never figure it out), but
the HTTP_POST_VARS hash is a bit strange.  Basically, your variables are
converted from the hash into normal variables:

phpinfo() shows something like this -
HTTP_POST_VARS["MyVariable"] = MyValue
MyVariable = MyValue

Referencing it like this doesn't work as expected:
if ($HTTP_POST_VARS["MyVariable"] == "MyValue")
{
}

However, referencing it like this does:
if ($MyVariable == "MyValue")
{
}

>I've searched the archives and have seen a few other people mention
>this problem but haven't seen any solutions posted. I've waisted best
>part of a day on this and it is driving me nuts. Xitami looks good,
>but if I can't get this resolved quickly I guess I'll move to Apache.

Apache is horribly unstable under Windows with PHP (especially with
mod-ssl).  I wasted an entire week re-building that piece of junk from
scratch using every option possible (I personally would write my own web
server if I had a choice between that and Apache - it's a good thing Xitami
exists).  Just thought you would like a heads-up.

>On another note why haven't the Archived Mailing lists been updated
>for many months?

Check the headers of this post for links to the new archives.

Hope this helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Dan Fisher)

Subject: [Xitami] Bad termination..
References: <200108172223.KAA19095@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <3B7EE9E5.FE4371B8@esite-me.net>

> >Also, I have noticed lately that when I make a change to Xitami,
> >terminate and attempt to restart, it complains that the port is already
> >in use.  I have to reboot the machine to get to work again.
> 
> You _probably_ won't have to reboot the machine providing whatever is
> using the port is stopped correctly.  But if you interupt a connection
> which Xitami thinks is open, then you may have to wait for the "closing
> connections" phase before you can restart it.
> 
> Try:
> 
> netstat -nr
> 
> from a command shell, and look to see if there are any lines for port
> 80 (http), particularly any that mention being in a CLOSE phase (or even
> "listening").
> 
> Typical timeouts is about 5 minutes or so.  Xitami tries to tell the
> operating system not to wait in this instance, but it may not get it
> right for every operating system.

Yes, it does show up as CLOSE_WAIT.  Is there any other way to speed up
the closing?  I have only recently been having this problem.  It has
worked fine in the past.  Is it possible that a variable setting could
have broken it??  

Dan

As long as you don't run mod-ssl, you will be fine (maybe one or two Apache
child process crashes a day).  If you run mod-ssl, watch out, mod-ssl,
mod-php (or even PHP in CGI mode), and Apache don't mix well (they crash
about once every 10 page requests).

>>>On another note why haven't the Archived Mailing lists been updated

List-Help: <mailto:xitami-request@lists.xitami.org?subject=help>
List-Post: <mailto:xitami@lists.xitami.org>
List-Subscribe: <http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami>,
	<mailto:xitami-request@lists.xitami.org?subject=subscribe>
List-Id: Xitami Users General Discussion <xitami.lists.xitami.org>
List-Unsubscribe: <http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami>,
	<mailto:xitami-request@lists.xitami.org?subject=unsubscribe>
List-Archive: <http://lists.xitami.org/pipermail/xitami/>

You want the "List-Archive" link.  If you can't read the headers in "The
Bat!" (Your mail client), then it is probably time to get something else.
I highly recommend Eudora Light v3.0.6 (I can't stand the interface on
anything newer from Qualcomm and all the other freeware clients can't do
everything Eudora can with the ease of Eudora - and 3.0.6 is about the only
non-HTML mail client out there anymore).

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Aug 19 06:43:00 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Sun, 19 Aug 2001 00:43:00 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Abnormal Program Termination
In-Reply-To: <5.0.2.1.0.20010818230717.017e0598@192.168.0.1>
References: <3B7EE9E5.FE4371B8@esite-me.net>
 <200108172223.KAA19095@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010819004300.007b1c30@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 11:14 PM 8/18/01 -0500, B. Solomon writeth:
> A little system information:
> 
> Pentium 233MMX
> 32-Megs of memory

Your main problem is probably right here.  Xitami has, IMO, not-so-great
memory management since it is generally built under MSVC++ for the various
Windows builds.  You are probably running out of memory (usually happens
when running CGIs like PHP) and then the MSVC library fails, thus Xitami
fails.  The library probably fails since it will generally lock itself in
real memory (so it can't be swapped out), then when you get enough locks
and zero memory free, bam!  Windows kills the offending application (which
is Xitami).

My suggestion in this case is to get more memory (my system has 384MB RAM -
you probably don't need that much if you run a dedicated server - my
machine is a high-end workstation/server) and something like MemTurbo or
RamIdle (both utilities can free up real RAM when it gets low).

> Windows 95 OSR2 with latest patches.
> Console reports nearly 9 megabytes of configuration usage (normal - system
>has about 200 virtual hosts).

I normally don't recommend RAM purchases, but if you run 200 VHosts, they
probably need more than 32MB under any circumstance (Windows needs about
24MB to run decently (at least 16MB to run), add 9MB to that and you have
0MB of real RAM free and are probably doing some major hard drive
swapping).  128MB with RamIdle set to recover RAM at 25MB free should
provide you, your users, and more importantly the OS some breathing room.

Hope this helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Aug 20 09:39:17 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 20 Aug 2001 20:39:17 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Any way to get xitami to DENY connections from specific IPs?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Jeff Hamblin" <jphamblin@home.net>
 of "Sun, 19 Aug 2001 23:36:22 MST." <003b01c12942$91fd6e10$0d00a8c0@dt1.sdca.home.com>
Message-ID: <200108200839.UAA07549@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <003b01c12942$91fd6e10$0d00a8c0@dt1.sdca.home.com>, "Jeff Hamblin" writes:
>[webmask in Xitami accepts, and sends forbidden]
>What I really want to do is deny any connection at all from certain IPs,
>just ignore them (sending no error message).
>Is this possible with 2.4d9?

No. What you want is a firewall; then you can configure it to drop
traffic from sites you don't like (and thus completely ignore them).

Because of the way that Xitami works it has to accept the connection to
find out who is at the other end, and at that point it'd be very rude to
just hang up on them, so it sends a HTTP-style response back.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Aug 21 04:23:55 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 21 Aug 2001 15:23:55 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Where do requests for GET /default.ida come from in access.log
In-Reply-To: Message from Iwski13@aol.com
 of "Mon, 20 Aug 2001 23:10:52 EDT." <e0.194ea16f.28b32b3d@aol.com>
Message-ID: <200108210323.PAA19968@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <e0.194ea16f.28b32b3d@aol.com>, Iwski13@aol.com writes:
>128.211.240.66 - - [20/Aug/2001:18:52:40 -0500] "GET /default.ida?XXXXXXXXXXXXX
>XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX
>XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX
>XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX%u9090%u6858%ucbd3%u7801%u
>9090%u6858%ucbd3%u7801%u9090%u6858%ucbd3%u7801%u9090%u9090%u8190%u00c3%u0003%u8
>b00%u531b%u53ff%u0078%u0000%u00=a%20 HTTP/1.0" 200 0 "" ""
>
>Does anybody know what that means?  

It's a CodeRed attempt.  The mainstream media have been talking about
this for about three weeks, and the worm has been around in various
forms for about a month or so.

>I get about 10 an hour and from different IP addresses, but most (not all) 
>start with 128.x.x.x  

CodeRedII (the varient in that log message) tries to infect machines
"close to home", ie in the same range of IP addresses as it is in.  So
you'll get a lot of them from the address block you are in.

Xitami isn't vulnerable to this worm (only IIS without patches can be
infected, but some other webservers crash), so it's merely an annoying
way to fill up your log files.

When all the IIS webserver administrators finally patch their machines,
clean them up, and reboot them, the problem will go away.  Given that
there's been three weeks of media publicity and there's still plenty of
infected machines around I wouldn't hold your breath.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

On which point, I find it perfectly reprehensible that someone could be
knowingly running a webserver and yet be unaware of the existence of Code
Red.  After all, the majority of infected instances of IIS exist because
their owners were blissfully unaware that the webserver had been
installed by default.

ANYONE running ANY sort of semi-permanently connected server should
ensure that they are up-to-date with CERT advisories for their platform;
it's a duty that they have to the integrity of the rest of the 'Net.

Incidentally, there should be a respite for a few days now: all the
machines infected with Code Red (1 or 2) are now (from the 20th of each
month) instead launching a DoS attack on the IP address that used to be
one of the servers forming www.whitehouse.gov.  This will continue until,
IIRC, the 28th, when the worm will go dormant; only to start another
month's attempt of infestation on the 1st.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Aug 21 10:51:38 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Patrick L. Olson)
Date: Tue, 21 Aug 2001 03:51:38 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] Perl support ?
References: <20010820125746.42098.qmail@web12905.mail.yahoo.com>

Nathan Rimmer wrote:
> 
> Yeah - apart from that ;-)
> 
> Cheers,
> Digsy
> 

You may also need this in your defaults.cfg file

[Cgi]
    Debug = "1"
    Exit-ok = "0"
    Form-query = "1"
    Full-name = "1"
    Timeout = "120"
    Wildcard = "1"

[Filter]
    . = "text/plain"
    .pl = "/usr/local/bin/perl"
    .php = "/usr/local/bin/php"
    .shtm = "perlssi"
    .shtml = "perlssi"
    .ssi = "perlssi"


hope it helps

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Aug 21 23:51:04 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 22 Aug 2001 10:51:04 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Port Problem?
In-Reply-To: Message from DMW <dwalker@netplicity.tzo.com>
 of "Tue, 21 Aug 2001 18:33:48 -0400." <n7bwqro47m116rt.210820011819@mail>
Message-ID: <200108212251.KAA28378@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <n7bwqro47m116rt.210820011819@mail>, DMW writes:
>So now I've configured Xitami to use port 5080 , although it is 
>displaying as port 5160 in the admin console, why is this?
>Does this mean I am actually using port 5160 ? 

Actually you've configured to use a port base of 5080, ie add 5080 to
all port numbers.  Hence 5160.  You probably want a port base of 5000.

>I've since asked TZO to relay my port 80 requests to port 5160( not 
>5080), and my website is coming up on the external WAN (Internet) as 
>per the norm, however (Good grief!) None of my website links off my 
>main page now work, only the main page displays. 

This will depend on how you do your links, and what their port
forwarding service does.  You may or may not need to explicitly include
the port number in the links.  (You will if you use absolute URLs in the
links and their port forwarding thing just sends a redirect; if they do
the port forward "properly" (proxy the connection), then you probably
shouldn't.)

Unless you can figure out what they're doing you might just have to
experiment and find out.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Aug 22 00:04:28 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 21 Aug 2001 19:04:28 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Port Problem?
References: <n7bwqro47m116rt.210820011819@mail>
Message-ID: <3B82E8FC.A30D12F6@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I've configured Xitami to use port 5080 , although it is displaying as port 5160 in the admin console, 

Xitami assumes port 80; the number you put in the config is ADDED to 80
to get the actual port. So "0" = Port 80; "5080" means Port 5160
(5080+80). 

This is noted in a comment if you edit the file by hand: 

    portbase=0                          #   e.g. 5000 for port 5080

In the Admin screens, HELP tells you: 

portbase - Defines the IP port base for the server. Add 80 to this to
calculate the actual port used for the HTTP service. For example, to run
the server on port 6080, define portbase as 6000. We use a portbase in
place of an absolute address so that multiple protocols (e.g. the FTP
server embedded into Xitami) can be managed as one unit. 
Default: 0 (zero) 

 -PRR

testcgi.exe is an executable program, not a perl script.   If you're
having trouble running perl scripts (a) make sure you have Perl
installed, (b) make sure Perl is in the PATH, (c) make sure your
perl scripts start with something like #! perl, and (d) check cgierr.log
for any error messages.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Aug 22 17:39:15 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Wed, 22 Aug 2001 12:39:15 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] CodeRed.worm and McAfee
References: <5.1.0.14.0.20010822154007.00a6b0c0@mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <3B83E033.5D98388C@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Fichier infect:
 C:\Xitami\DEBUG\request.log
 Nom du virus:
 W32/CodeRed.worm

> Any explanation ? There is a potential risk ?

The only odd thing is: you should have been getting these warnings all
month. Everybody with any software that uses port 80 (the usual HTTP
protocol port) has been getting hits from CodeRed machines. 

If this is the first time you've run your virus scanner since July, then
that's OK. 

> GET /default.ida?XXXXXX............

Yes, that IS the virus. (And thanks for cutting off the extra 3000 bytes
in this email.) Send that request to an un-patched MS IIS server, and it
will be infected. Except that odds are that ALL the IIS servers in the
world are already infected. 

Having that virus sitting in your log files is quite safe. 

In fact it is a little silly for your virus checker to warn you. CodeRed
does not live in files, because it can only infect via an HTTP request
to a IIS server. A copy of CodeRed in a log file means that you are
studying the virus, or it tried to infect you and failed, and your
server simply noted the "bad request". 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug 23 16:35:36 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 23 Aug 2001 11:35:36 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] axs script
References: <3B82416F.F725C297@sovik.no>
Message-ID: <3B8522C8.2F7C95D@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Does someone have the AXS Site Tracking System (http://www.xav.com/) up and running. ...whenever i try ax.pl (the script that actually counts the visits) I'm always getting...  ax.pl - working okay - no logging command received - use ?debugme query string for more info. 

You don't normally call ax.pl directly. If you do, you get that message. 

You embed ax.pl in an IMG (or SSI) tag on the page(s) you want counted.
There is a link to instructions in localhost/cgi-bin/axs/ax.pl?debugme

I could not get it to work at first. There seem to be typos in the
documentation. I use Xitami but this isn't an Xitami issue. 

"if you are not using SSI, place this code on each of your HTML pages:

 <SCRIPT LANGUAGE="JavaScript">
 <!--
   document.write("<IMG SRC=\"\cgi-bin\axs\ax.pl?trans.gif&ref=");
   document.write(document.referrer);
   document.write("\" HEIGHT=1 WIDTH=1>");
 // -->
 </SCRIPT><NOSCRIPT>
 <IMG SRC="\cgi-bin\axs\ax.pl?trans.gif" HEIGHT="1" WIDTH="1">
 </NOSCRIPT>  

I'm pretty sure the DOS-type path slashes "\" MUST be changed to
unix/perl/javascript type slashes "/". (Even on Windows.) However, the
escape slashes in front of quotes must be back\slashes. 

This is my interpretation. I assume (for testing) that all clients have
javascript so I only have to mess with one part. (I also highlighted the
"invisible" image so I could verify it was being shown.)

 <SCRIPT LANGUAGE="JavaScript">
 <!--
   document.write("<IMG SRC=\"/cgi-bin/axs/ax.pl?trans.gif&ref=");
   document.write(document.referrer);
   document.write("\" HEIGHT=10 WIDTH=10 border=2>");
 // -->
 </SCRIPT>

Since this seems to be a problem with AXS's skimpy instructions, not any
interaction with Xitami, you should probably seek further help on their
support forum http://www.xav.com/scripts/forum.pl

  -PRR

I tried it with Xitami and it worked pretty much right from the zip. You 
have to make sure that you are pointing to the correct location. The AXS 
default calls for 

document.write("<IMG SRC="\axs\ax.pl?trans.gif&ref=");

This ASSUMES that you have AXS installed in http://whatever.com/axs

Anywhere else, and you will have to change the directory/location.

I also did notice that it didn't matter if I used \ or /...

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Aug 24 00:23:28 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 23 Aug 2001 19:23:28 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] mysql/php on a Win2k under Xitami
References: <15a1iN-1mfdNwC@fmrl06.sul.t-online.com>
Message-ID: <3B859070.76EB5D5A@rci.rutgers.edu>

> The mysql items needed to connect from a domain / website to it are a "host" (server), the database name, username and password ... and it is the first one (the "host" / server) which I was wondering about 

Ah. 

It "should" work to specify "localhost" as the "remote" server, and TCP
as the protocol if that is needed.

Then when PHP opens a connection to the "remote server" named
"localhost", the TCP stack re-directs it to the same machine. Change
"localhost" to "server2.your_isp.com" for production. 

In some cases, "localhost" isn't correctly specified. "127.0.0.1" should
also work to mean "this same machine". 

In some cases, for no good reason, Windows will insist on connecting to
an outside DNS server even for hosts it has in its own "hosts" file.
Microsoft just doesn't understand DNS or TCP. It may work if you unplug
your modem phone line and wait patiently for it to give up trying to
reach an external DNS server. You can check that by seeing if opening
"localhost" in your browser works without Windows trying to reach out
for DNS service. 

 -PRR

Only Windows NT/2000 machines running IIS 4/5 are vulnerable to the
attack.

Don't wait for your ISP to start blocking ports. Write to them now
telling them that you do NOT run a web server that can be exploited by
Code Red. Tell them that if they block HTTP requests that you will find
another ISP who is more attuned to the real world.

As Arlo Guthrie said, "if enough of us get together they'll think its a
movement". Don't let your ISP determine what gets to your server, it is
not their place. This is an administrative issue, not an ISP issue. Take
the initiative. Hit them where it hurts, paying the bill.

It is just like voting in the states, the powers that be are there to
serve us, not us there to serve them.

Hello,

your PATH-Variable should reflect your Perl-Installation.
On my System this is:

F:\>path
PATH=D:\Programme\Apple\Developer\Executables\Utilities;D:\Pro
gramme\Apple\Devel
oper\Executables;D:\Programme\Apple\Local\Library\Executables;
D:\Programme\Apple
\Library\JDK\bin;D:\Programme\Apple\Library\Executables;D:\Progr
amme\Perl\bin\;D
:\Perl\5.6.0\bin\;C:\WINNT\system32;C:\WINNT;D:\Programme\cyg
win\bin;D:\Programm
e\cygwin\usr\bin;D:\Programme\cygwin\usr\local\bin;D:\Programme\
Python20\;D:\Pro
gramme\jdk1.2\bin;D:\gnu\usr\local\wbin;C:\Programme\texmf\mikte
x\bin;C:\Program
me\localtexmf;C:\Programme\Symantec\pcAnywhere\;D:\Programm
e\Komodo\python\;D:\P
rogramme\cygwin\bin;D:\Programme\ssl\bin;D:\Programme\gnu\usr\
local\wbin;D:\Prog
ramme\vunix

If you add  #!/usr/bin/perl (the exact path to perl not neccesary)  to 
the first line of perl-scripts, xitami/perl should work with any 
virualhost.


You don't need these free mailing scripts; better do your own:


#!/usr/bin/perl 

use MIME::Lite;

$mailhost = "someMailAlias";
$From = 'someOne@somewhere.net';
$To = 'anotherOne@outside.net';
$Subject = 'mailing';
$text .= "$something\n";
 MIME::Lite -> send('smtp', $mailhost, Timeout => 60);
 $msg = MIME::Lite -> new(From => $From, To => $To, Subject 
=> $Subject, Data => $text);
$msg -> send;
undef $msg;



So long,

Peter

>> should i use:
>> .pl=c:\perl\bin\perl.exe
>> or
>> .pl = "c:\perl\bin\perl.exe" ??
>
>First try without. If that does not work, then try the first line (without
>the "" marks). I'm not sure if you need them or not - I don't use them.

The quote marks, when used in the Filters section will cause Xitami to
execute the executable called '"c:\perl\bin\perl.exe"' instead of
'c:\perl\bin\perl.exe'.  It took me a while to figure this one out myself.

Hope this helps!

An interesting thing... I took so long to write back because I wanted to 
see if it was just my imagination.

I was mistaken, I had 64-megs of memory afterall.  But here's what I 
did:  I simply opened the WBA, changed a setting, and then changed it back 
to its original value, saved, then restarted.  The server has been much 
much more stable since.  I didn't add a single stick of memory either and 
that is *all* I did.

Just thought you'd like to know...

B. Solomon
wire@austin.rr.com



At 12:43 AM 8/19/2001 -0500, you wrote:
>At 11:14 PM 8/18/01 -0500, B. Solomon writeth:
> > A little system information:
> >
> > Pentium 233MMX
> > 32-Megs of memory
>
>Your main problem is probably right here.  Xitami has, IMO, not-so-great
>memory management since it is generally built under MSVC++ for the various
>Windows builds.  You are probably running out of memory (usually happens
>when running CGIs like PHP) and then the MSVC library fails, thus Xitami
>fails.  The library probably fails since it will generally lock itself in
>real memory (so it can't be swapped out), then when you get enough locks
>and zero memory free, bam!  Windows kills the offending application (which
>is Xitami).
>
>My suggestion in this case is to get more memory (my system has 384MB RAM -
>you probably don't need that much if you run a dedicated server - my
>machine is a high-end workstation/server) and something like MemTurbo or
>RamIdle (both utilities can free up real RAM when it gets low).
>
> > Windows 95 OSR2 with latest patches.
> > Console reports nearly 9 megabytes of configuration usage (normal - system
> >has about 200 virtual hosts).
>
>I normally don't recommend RAM purchases, but if you run 200 VHosts, they
>probably need more than 32MB under any circumstance (Windows needs about
>24MB to run decently (at least 16MB to run), add 9MB to that and you have
>0MB of real RAM free and are probably doing some major hard drive
>swapping).  128MB with RamIdle set to recover RAM at 25MB free should
>provide you, your users, and more importantly the OS some breathing room.
>
>Hope this helps!
>
>
>            Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
>Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
>                   http://www.shininglightpro.com/
>
>--
>Xitami Users Mailing List -- For Xitami support
>To unsubscribe: http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Aug 25 06:22:41 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 25 Aug 2001 17:22:41 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] CodeRed.worm and McAfee
In-Reply-To: Message from DanLM <Dan_LM@yahoo.com>
 of "Wed, 22 Aug 2001 15:54:52 +0200." <5.1.0.14.0.20010822154007.00a6b0c0@mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <200108250522.RAA07794@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <5.1.0.14.0.20010822154007.00a6b0c0@mail.yahoo.com>, DanLM writes:
>I received an alert from my McAfee antivirus, I know that using xitami web 
>server the virus can't input on my Windows95 system. The message was: (in 
>french)
>
>Fichier infect:
>C:\Xitami\DEBUG\request.log
>Nom du virus:
>W32/CodeRed.worm

Log files are just that -- logs.  They might happen to contain a copy of
the virus (because it's sent as one big URL request), but in the log
file it's basically inert.  There's no way it can run, or spread or
anything.

It sounds like McAfee antivirus is just looking for patterns which
happen to match viruses, without any real consideration for why they
might be there, or what that might mean.  Hence the false alarms.

You might want to consider whether you want Xitami in debug mode (that's
how request.log is generated), as it can generate bit log files, but
otherwise you don't have a problem).  CodeRed (and its variations) can
only affect Microsoft IIS servers that haven't been patched against it.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Aug 27 10:37:55 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 27 Aug 2001 21:37:55 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Bad termination..
In-Reply-To: Message from Dan Fisher <djf@esite-me.net>
 of "Sat, 18 Aug 2001 15:19:17 MST." <3B7EE9E5.FE4371B8@esite-me.net>
Message-ID: <200108270937.VAA10331@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3B7EE9E5.FE4371B8@esite-me.net>, Dan Fisher writes:
>> >Also, I have noticed lately that when I make a change to Xitami,
>> >terminate and attempt to restart, it complains that the port is already
>> >in use.  I have to reboot the machine to get to work again.
>>
>> [need to wait for connection closing timeout: netstat -nr tells you
>> if this is happening]
>
>Yes, it does show up as CLOSE_WAIT.  Is there any other way to speed up
>the closing?  

Alas, no.  It's the TCP/IP timeout.

However it only occurs (in my experience) if there are
_open_connections_ at the time that you close Xitami down; if there are
no open connections, then there's nothing to have to go through the
timeout.

So if you have the time to do it, checking for open connections 
(netstat -nr, look for connected type messages on that port), before
closing Xitami may make it easier to restart.

We'll keep this issue in mind; it maybe that there's an issue with the
way it's telling the OS "hey, it's okay to let the program restart
automatically" under some operating systems.  (Xitami does try to do
this, and it's definitely working under Linux.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Aug 27 10:41:26 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 27 Aug 2001 21:41:26 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] CGI program can't call FindWindow() ?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Lee Stewart" <LeeStewart@bigfoot.com>
 of "Fri, 17 Aug 2001 23:35:50 -0400." <BHEDLLPJFABBFBAIOHGOMEFOCJAA.LeeStewart@bigfoot.com>
Message-ID: <200108270941.VAA10472@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <BHEDLLPJFABBFBAIOHGOMEFOCJAA.LeeStewart@bigfoot.com>, "Lee Stewart" writes:
>I have a CGI program that needs to query another program that's running on
>the server.  I'm trying to get the title of the app using FindWindow() and
>GetWindowText().  My program works fine, but fails when running as a CGI
>program ("The specified module could not be found").
>
>Is there something weird about the way that Xitami calls a CGI program?

Possibly.  Xitami calls the program as, IIRC, a console program.  If
Windows is anything like OS/2 in terms of calling API, this will mean
that it can't call "windows" like functions -- such as
FindWindow()/GetWindowText().  

One thing you might want to try is having a small batch file that Xitami
can run as the CGI which then runs your program.  That way
command.com/cmd.exe will be involved, which does some hunting around to
figure out what type of program to run, and starting it the right way.

>I'm new to the mailing list - is there a searchable archive?

There's a mailing list archive at:

http://lists.xitami.org/pipermail/xitami/

but alas it isn't searchable at the moment.  (It's on our list of things
to do, along with getting the old archives and the new archives merged
together.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Aug 27 11:01:29 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 27 Aug 2001 22:01:29 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] RE: POST troubles (longish)
In-Reply-To: Message from Boyan Brezinsky <boyan@sanbolic.com>
 of "Mon, 16 Jul 2001 17:45:09 +0300." <01C10E1F.0F9877F0.boyan@sanbolic.com>
Message-ID: <200108271001.WAA11259@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <01C10E1F.0F9877F0.boyan@sanbolic.com>, Boyan Brezinsky writes:
>In the non-working case the generated output is (from *.flt):
>X-Powered-By: PHP/4.0.4
>Location: main.php3?menuAction=boMyDCL.show
>Set-Cookie: DCLINFO=1/0/dfe2c07de313f0d7ca27146e068767f1/en/default
>Set-Cookie: DCLTYPEMENU=0
>Content-type: text/html
>[....]
>As you can see, the difference is in the "Location:" header. The obvious 
>reason is that Xitami can't find the file specified in the Location header 
>and returns 404.

Ah.  Xitami basically expects that there will be an absolute reference
in the Location: line, and assumes that anything without a leading "/"
is in the root directory.  Hence the behaviour your saw.  

Other webservers are more forgiving (or more accurate, but AFAICT this
is an extension) and try the referenced document in the same directory
as the one that generated the reference.

IIRC we've already got a bug against this issue, and when someone gets
the time we'll try to make the Location: handling a little smarter.

The Meta refresh works in this instance because it relies on the web
browser to do the reloading, and the web browser has its own ideas about
defaults.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Hi Brad,

This is an old one that I fell into as well. Simply move php.exe and php4ts.dll
into the Xitami directory (or possibly php4ts.dll to winnt\system32\ or
equivalent depending on your windows flavour) and remove the paths from the
beginning of the Xitami filter line entry.

Re-start Xiami and all will being to function as expected, one day when I have
time I'll sit down & see why this is so :-).

I was given this info from somebody else on this mailing list, it appears fairly
frequently.

Best of Luck,

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Aug 29 08:54:46 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 29 Aug 2001 19:54:46 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Virtual Host Wizard Confusion
In-Reply-To: Message from Gordon Wong <gordonw@interchange.ubc.ca>
 of "Tue, 28 Aug 2001 13:18:42 MST." <3.0.6.32.20010828131842.00b64900@137.82.27.14>
Message-ID: <200108290754.TAA08353@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3.0.6.32.20010828131842.00b64900@137.82.27.14>, Gordon Wong writes:
>For CGI-BIN directory I want to use the common
>cgi-bin directory in c:\xitami\cgi-bin so I entered "/cgi-bin".

If you are configuring the "cgi-bin" setting (which is the actual
directory you want to use), and you enter "/cgi-bin", then Xitami will
expect that you mean "/cgi-bin", which under Windows translates to
"c:\cgi-bin" (assuming you're on C: drive).

Since that wasn't what you wanted, I'd suggest you enter either the
directory you wanted "c:\xitami\cgi-bin"; or leave it at the default
setting of "./cgi-bin", which means that providing you run Xitami from
the Xitami directory.

The cgi-url should be set to "/cgi-bin", if you want "..../cgi-bin/..." 
in your CGI URLs; this too is the default.

The defaults really are intended to be sensible, ya know :-)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug 30 00:55:38 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Thu, 30 Aug 2001 09:55:38 +1000
Subject: [Xitami] PHP4 Installation Problems
Message-ID: <4A256AB7.0083BB72.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>


Hi Peter,

There's no need at all to alter the extension settings in the php.ini file
unless you atually move the directory the extenstions are placed in. php parses
the php.ini file at startup and looks there expicilty to load extensions.
There's also no need to place the extension directory in the path (although it
shouldn't do any harm).

With php.exe in the Xitami directory (eg if Xitami is installed in C:\Xitami
this is where php.exe should be placed - NOT in any subdirectory such as
C:\Xitami\cgi-bin etc) the filter should simply be set to

.php php.exe

without any paths.

I was assuming from your original post that you weren't getting error
messages... just blank pages, is this correct ???

Regards, Paul

> directory in the path (although it shouldn't do any harm).
> 
> With php.exe in the Xitami directory (eg if Xitami is installed in
> C:\Xitami this is where php.exe should be placed - NOT in any
> subdirectory such as C:\Xitami\cgi-bin etc) the filter should simply
> be set to
> 
> .php php.exe
> 
> without any paths.
> 
> I was assuming from your original post that you weren't getting error
> messages... just blank pages, is this correct ???


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug 30 02:24:59 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Thu, 30 Aug 2001 11:24:59 +1000
Subject: [Xitami] PHP4 Installation Problems
Message-ID: <4A256AB8.00080E68.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>


Brad,

No, a path entry for php isn't necessary (but it might be worth trying at this
point !), I even went to the extent of moving php4ts.dll from the Xitami
directory to the wnint\system32 directory & deleting php.exe & php4ts.dll from
the C:\php directory & all still functions perfectly.

Correction - I found out what is happening, - instead of just accepting that my
installation was working I had a poke around to see if I could reproduce the
'blank page problem' .... it happens when php.exe can't locate php4ts.dll, if
you do a 'view source' on the blank page you will see that php has produced the
headers then given up when unable to load it's main dll.

It just so happened that when I moved php.exe to C:\Xitami I also moved
php4ts.dll which allowed it to be found. Now I've moved php.exe to c:\php &
altered the filter to point to c:\php\php.exe and all works fine when php4ts.dll
is placed in winnt\system32.

My suggestion - place php4ts.dll in the winnt\system32 directory, it will always
get found there.

Best of luck, Paul

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug 30 03:53:31 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Thu, 30 Aug 2001 12:53:31 +1000
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami PHP UNIX
Message-ID: <4A256AB8.00102960.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>


You can compile php as a cgi. If you want a compiled in server extension (WSX)
you would have to write the interface yourself, take a look at the various sub
directories of the php 'sapi' directories to see how various server api's are
implimented - unfortuately Xitami isn't one of them.

Quite frankly I wouldn't take this route as LRWP is a fairly simple protocal &
is likely to cause you far less grief than WSX. You could use the fastcgi
interface in php's sapi/fastcgi directory as a starting point & just replace the
necessary bits with calls to the Xitami lrwp functions that are supplied with
the Xitami source. This is likely to give you far fewer headaches & if you write
a simple process manager to manager / kill/ re-start the lrwp php process you
will have a very robust server & php is such a joy to program in, you get the
best of both worlds.

Regards, Paul

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug 30 05:21:11 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (MATA Tech)
Date: Thu, 30 Aug 2001 00:21:11 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami/PHP Success and Instructions
In-Reply-To: <3B8D749B.18825.6F2588@localhost>
References: <4A256AB8.00080E68.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>
Message-ID: <3B8D86F7.31367.B6DCC5@localhost>

I did it!  PHP is installed in collaboration with Xitami and my Win32 
box!!!  But, what would my success be worth if I didn't share the 
steps and Xitami foibles with all of you who are equally puzzled! :)

1.  Xitami, in combination with PHP (and perhaps a fair bit of my 
own human error) requires that any virtual directory be named 
exactly as the name of the file folder in which that particular 
website is stored.  For instance, a site folder at c:\greene_find_out 
cannot be registered with a virtual host name of greene.  It must be 
greene_find_out.  That was the cause of my problems all along!

2.  The way I discovered this malfunction (some of which is 
probably mine.... along with poorly written documentation) was to 
change the php.ini line that reads this:
error_log=

to this:
error_log=c:\xitami\php_error.txt

This will create a log file named php_error.txt in your Xitami 
directory.  Every time something goes wrong during the 
instantiation of PHP, it will append the error report to this file.

I hope this helps others who are having problems installing PHP.  I 
apologize if my explanation is scattered.  It is late in the evening, 
and I have been agonising over installing PHP for the past 24 
hours.... and that's one obsession I can do without! :)

Sincerely,
Brad Smith,
Social Design Technologies
mata@matatech.tzo.com

When you state that you 'create a virtual directory named 'greene', do you mean
simply a directory under 'Xitami\webpages' or are you creating a virtual host ?

There is a simple way to see if php is working. Open a DOS box, go to the
directory containing 'today.php' and type 'path to php.exe'\php today.php (eg
c:\xitami\php today.php). You should be blessed with the expected output from
your php script on the console.

I installed php way before Xitami so I didn't have the option of telling the
installer about Xitami, however the setup is just a matter of setting the Xitami
php filter & moving 2 files, php.exe & php4ts.dll.

In any case the virtual directory question may be the most important.

Regards, Paul

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Aug 30 09:36:41 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Thu, 30 Aug 2001 18:36:41 +1000
Subject: [Xitami] PHP4 Installation Problems
Message-ID: <4A256AB8.002F97B5.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>



Hi Peter,

Those lines look okay IF they really do both begin with semi-colons (;) then
they will simply be treated as comment lines.

The installer must have mangled them from the default line which is ...

;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;
; Paths and Directories ;
;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;
include_path   =               ; UNIX: "/path1:/path2"  Windows: "\path1;\path2"
doc_root  =    ; the root of the php pages, used only if nonempty

This is how my system is setup, because I don't use any implicit includes - this
 explicitly sets the default include
path to null  instead of using any compiled in default. You might try this
syntax & see how much mileage you get.

As I said if the lines begin with a ; then they will be treated as comments, I
would be likely to check the line FOLLOWING
the line the error is reported on, i.e. Line 315

Also if you set the following values On earlier in the ini file you make get
helpful messages displayed in your
browser, 'display_startup_errors defaults' to Off

display_errors =    On
display_startup_errors = On

Also, although it appears you may already have 'log_errors' set to On (since
you're getting server error logs) , I would
check to make sure 'log_errors' is in fact set to On.

Although I think you've almost cracked it, another thing I've found is that you
will get the blank pages if php.exe can't locate
php4ts.dll - it should either be in the Xitami directory along with php.exe
(since that is Xitami's cwd when starting php) or in
c:\winnt\system32. In fact I've found that php.exe can be left in c:\php (and
the Xitami filter entry altered to match php.exe's
location of course) if php4ts.dll is placed in c:\winnt\system32 .

Hope that's enough to nudge you in the right direction...

Regards, Paul

Hi,

Don't know if this helps, but i had same problem installing php with Xitami
under Windows... and it was -yes- an unbeliavable incredible minor problem:

I had this in the filter configuration:

[Filter]
    .php=F:\PROGRAMAS\PHP\php.exe

and had to change it to:

[Filter]
    .php=F:\PROGRA~1\PHP\php.exe

Don't ask me why... but it worked after this minor change.

Regards,
Rui Leite

--start--

I had this in the filter configuration:
